1932.12.24

Today's Main Points of This Newspaper

Domestic: The Central Political Council hands over the cases submitted by the Third Plenary Session to various groups for review; Chen Guohui is executed by firing squad in Fuzhou; Chairman Chiang Kai-shek summons senior military officers in Nanjing for instruction.

Foreign: Roosevelt replies to Hoover, declining to send representatives to discuss war debts; The French Chamber of Deputies expresses confidence in the new cabinet; The Japanese Diet opens today.

Shanghai: Sun Ke, Wu Chaoshu, and others return to Shanghai; Li Du requests the establishment of military postal services in Jilin; The Municipal Government receives four million eight hundred thousand yuan in national reconstruction bonds.

The Japanese Army's Plot in Rehe Grows Tighter, With Large Forces Concentrated on the Border Awaiting Orders

Plans to Attack Chifeng and Chengde in Two Directions

Using Chinese Traitors and Mongolian Bandits as Special Forces

Sending Planes to Rehe for Reconnaissance Daily

The 9th and 8th Divisions Transported from Heilongjiang to Suizhong

(Beiping) After Su Bingwen's army retreated into Russian territory, the Japanese military aggression in North Manchuria came to an end, and their sights gradually turned to Rehe. The 9th and 8th Divisions have already been transported from Heilongjiang to the Suizhong area, and a light railway is being built from Suizhong to a certain place on the Rehe border in preparation for invading Rehe. It is reported that the Japanese plan to organize Chinese traitors Cheng Guorui, Li Jichun, and Fang Yongchang into three army corps to act as special forces to disrupt Rehe. Recently, Japanese planes have frequently flown over Rehe for reconnaissance. Some time ago, when a certain military officer from our side was traveling from Rehe to Beiping by car, a Japanese plane chased after him for several hours before leaving. The situation in Rehe is becoming increasingly tense, and the people of the country should pay close attention. Tang has expressed his determination to resist Japan and has increased defenses in the Nanling area. Feng Zhanhai's troops have also recently been replenished and will support Rehe. (23rd Dispatch)

Japanese Troops Stationed in Jinzhou Transported Towards Rehe

(Beiping) Zhu Qinglan returned to Beiping after inspecting the Rehe border and said that the Japanese are actively invading Rehe. They are now organizing a puppet army, led by remnants of the Zhili-Shandong clique such as Cheng Guorui, to act as vanguards in attacking Rehe, and are buying over local Mongolian bandits and hooligans to disturb the Rehe border. They are buying up food from the people in the Chaoyang area at high prices. Recently, they have been building several long-distance automobile roads from Jinzhou to the Rehe border. The 8th Division and the Suzuki Division stationed in Jinzhou have been transporting towards the Rehe border for days, with the aim of: 1) Advancing north from Chaoyang to attack Chifeng; 2) Advancing west from Chaoyang to attack Chengde. Our front-line Dong Futing Brigade is still in Nanling, and the Japanese front line is in Chaoyang. The distance between the two sides is very close. Feng Zhanhai's troops, numbering over ten thousand, are stationed in the Rehe border area, and most of them are cavalry. (23rd Dispatch)

Military Vehicles Transported from Shenyang to Jinzhou

(Beiping) A telegram from Qinhuangdao states that two thousand military vehicles have been transported from Shenyang to Jinzhou by the Japanese army, in preparation for attacking Rehe. (23rd Dispatch)

(Beiping) A dispatch from Shenyang states that the Japanese are preparing many small trucks in Shenyang to be converted for military use in wartime. The Japanese treat the local puppet army quite well, with all uniforms being like those of the military police, and salaries doubled compared to before, in order to reduce anti-Japanese sentiment. (23rd Dispatch)

Launching an Attack Under the Pretext of the Ishimoto Incident

(Tokyo) According to Japanese sources, the Ministry of the Army has concentrated a large force in the Rehe area awaiting orders, and is scheduled to attack Rehe within days. It is said that the Japanese army is using the pretext that Ishimoto Kennosuke, entrusted by the Kwantung Army, carried secret military orders to contact Tang Yulin on July 17 of this year, and has not been heard from since. It is believed that he has been shot by our righteous army, so the Japanese army has decided to launch a general attack on Rehe, to eliminate the righteous army as revenge for Ishimoto's death. (23rd, China Allied Press)

(Tokyo) Regarding Ishimoto Kennosuke, the liaison officer of the Kwantung Army who was kidnapped by the volunteer army near Chaoyang Temple on July 17, there have been various rumors about his fate. According to a public announcement received a few days ago, it seems that he was killed near Chengde, Rehe. If the military authorities confirm the truth, they will take decisive action. (23rd, Dentsu Telegram)

Tang Yulin and Others Vow to Defend the Territory to the Death

(Beiping) Zhu Qinglan and others previously visited and inspected the righteous armies in the Rehe area. During the meeting of local military and civilians convened in Chaoyang, the representatives made speeches, roughly divided into three points: 1) Resist Japanese goods; 2) Do not be seduced by the Japanese to avoid the continuation of the Fushun Pingdingshan incident; 3) Military and civilians cooperate to resist Japan unanimously. The representatives left Chaoyang that night. Upon hearing the news, the Japanese army sent several planes the next morning to fly over Chaoyang for reconnaissance and bombing. Tang Yulin and Dong Futing, the brigade commander of the garrison in Rehe, are all determined to defend the territory to the death. (23rd Dispatch)

(Beiping) The Municipal Party Headquarters telegraphed Tang Yulin, requesting him to strive to resist Japan. (23rd Dispatch)

(Jinan) The Provincial Party Headquarters and various people's organizations telegraphed Tang Yulin on the 22nd, stating that "The Northeast has fallen for more than a year in an instant. Your province controls the throat of Guanwai and is the shield of North China. The ambition of the tyrannical Japanese has been more than a day. Fortunately, your Excellency's handling has been appropriate, and this first line of national defense has been preserved. Your great achievements are admired by the people of the country. Recently, it has been heard that the tyrannical Japanese are gathering heavy troops on the Rehe border, and General Lao will launch a large-scale internal invasion. I hope you will supervise your generals and soldiers to strictly guard the border and not lightly abandon an inch of land. The people of our province will do their best in all aspects of spirit and material as a backup for your Excellency. This is respectfully reported in a telegram, and I hope you will appreciate it." (23rd Dispatch)

Puppet National Salvation Army Recruits into a Brigade

(Beiping) The number of Japanese aircraft in Jinzhou has increased to nine, coming and going erratically. The infantry and artillery are still each a regiment. Li Jichun, the leader of the puppet National Salvation Army, has recruited a brigade in various counties, with plans to organize six brigades, adopting a three-regiment system with attached special forces. In order to buy people's hearts, the Japanese side has distributed some disaster relief funds to various villages in Jin County, but the merchants and civilians still suffer from Japanese oppression, and hope that we will recover the lost land as soon as possible. The Jin County train is suspended, with a row of empty cars. Many Japanese military officers' families are sent eastward, and many Japanese merchants are also moving. The Japanese army is always afraid whenever it fights with the righteous army. Its planes immediately fly away when they encounter rifle and machine gun fire. Every morning, Japanese soldiers in Jincheng go to the station and the Jiaoda Courtyard to avoid attacks on the city by the righteous army. (23rd Dispatch)

He Zhuguo Arrives in Beiping to Meet Zhang and Inquire About Plans

Will Return to Yuguan in Two or Three Days

(Tianjin) He Zhuguo passed through Tianjin to Beiping on the morning of the 23rd. According to reports, he met with Zhang to report on the resolution of the recent Japanese armored vehicle incursion into Yuguan. The situation outside Guan is now becoming increasingly tense, and he inquired about plans from Zhang. He will return to Yuguan in two or three days. (23rd Dispatch)

(Beiping) He Zhuguo arrived in Beiping this morning to meet with Zhang, reporting on the Yuguan incident and inquiring about everything. He will stay in Beiping for two or three days before returning to Yuguan to defend against any incidents. (23rd Dispatch)

The Authorities in Beiping and Tianjin Prevent Japanese Provocations

Yu Xuezhong Said... Sufficient Preparations Have Been Made

The End of the Year is Most Noteworthy

(Tianjin) Yu Xuezhong told reporters on the 23rd that reports that Zhang will convene a meeting of North China generals in Beiping are incorrect. Han Fuqu and Shen Honglie went to Beiping to discuss the Yantai defense issue. Rumors have been rife recently due to the looming war clouds in eastern Rehe. If the Japanese army attacks Rehe, it will certainly provoke Beiping and Tianjin to restrain our army. I have made sufficient preparations, and troops can be mobilized at any time, and I am determined to fulfill my responsibility to defend the territory and protect the people. The end of the Gregorian calendar year and the end of the Lunar New Year are the most noteworthy periods. (23rd Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Yu Xuezhong is scheduled to inspect the garrison along the Jinpu Railway starting on the 25th, and a special train has been prepared. (23rd Dispatch)

A Japanese Plane Was Shot Down by the Righteous Army

Of the Seven People on Board: One Seriously Injured, Six Killed

(Changchun) According to today's news, a Japanese plane bombed the righteous army, but was shot by the righteous army's gunfire. The plane was forced to crash, and the engine exploded. Of the seven people on board, six were killed on the spot, and one was seriously injured but not yet dead. Among them, four were officers. (23rd, Reuters)

(Tokyo) The Japanese military authorities are now preparing to attack the volunteer army to clear the area east of Hailin. The Japanese authorities have therefore negotiated with the Soviet Russian consulate in Harbin on the matter of transporting troops to Wuzhan. It is heard that the Russian consul has requested instructions from Moscow and is awaiting a reply. (23rd, Reuters)

Many Properties of Northeast Officials Confiscated

"Residence of a Certain Important Person in Jinzhou Actually Converted into a Japanese Brothel"

(Beiping) The Japanese will confiscate the property of Northeast officials and convert their houses into dormitories for puppet officials. The Japanese have recently confiscated the residences of important Northeast figures in Jinzhou and along the Fengshan Line, and have mostly converted them into brothels. The residence of a certain important person in Jinzhou has actually been converted into a Japanese brothel. (23rd Dispatch)

Yang Sen Agrees to Establish a Sichuan Government Rectification Committee

(Nanjing) Yang Sen telegraphed Zhang Qun on the 18th, expressing his strong agreement with the proposal to establish a Sichuan Government Rectification Committee to handle the aftermath of Sichuan affairs, and hopes that it will be realized soon. (23rd, Central News Agency)

The Special Committee of Nineteen Nations Will Draft a General Report on the Shandong Incident

Forcing Both Parties to Accept According to Article 15 of the Covenant

Otherwise, Sanctions Will Be Applied Using Article 16 of the Covenant

(Nanjing) The Special Committee of Nineteen Nations extended the meeting to January 16 of next year due to the inability to resolve the issue of whether or not to recognize the puppet organization. According to diplomatic sources, Geneva is currently secretly active in the hope of finding a way that can be agreed upon by China and Japan, but it is feared that it will be difficult to achieve results. It is heard that the Special Committee of Nineteen Nations will draft a general report based on Article 15, Paragraph 4 of the Covenant, forcing both parties to accept it. If any party refuses to accept the recommendations of the general report, sanctions will be applied using Article 16 of the Covenant. The diplomatic community is now paying close attention to the content of the general report. (23rd, Central News Agency)

The Central Political Council Passes the Principles of the Industrial Plan

Supplements for the Heads of the Legal and Education Branches Not Discussed Yesterday

Cases Submitted by the Third Plenary Session Handed Over to Various Groups for Review

(Nanjing) The Central Political Council held its 336th meeting at 3:00 p.m. on the 23rd, attended by members Chiang Kai-shek, Yu Youren, Wu Jingheng, Zhang Ji, Chen Gongbo, Huang Shaoxiong, Wu Tiecheng, Zeng Yangfu, Wang Zhengting, He Yingqin, Chu Minyi, and over forty others. Chairman Chiang resolved the following important cases:

1) The cases submitted by the Third Plenary Session will be reviewed by various standing committee members according to their nature.

2) The proposal by Dai Chuanxian regarding the various administrative systems related to the examination system, matters that should be promoted or reformed, will be reviewed by the Education and Legal Groups.

3) The proposal by Dai Chuanxian to review and approve the principles of revising the Examination Law, the Examination Supervision Law, and the Organizational Law of the Examination Committee will be reviewed by the Education and Legal Groups.

4) Tang Youren and others reported on the review of the plan proposed by the Ministry of Industry to reorganize and develop industry. As a result, the principles were approved and handed over to the competent authorities to handle them according to established regulations and discretion.

5) Chen Gongbo's proposal to participate in the Chicago Exposition and collect the standards for exhibits from the Chinese government's pavilion will be handled accordingly.

He said that the honest cooperation and common survival and prosperity between "Manchukuo" and Japan are necessary to ensure peace in the Far East, which is why Japan was the first to recognize the new nation. Puyi responded by welcoming Mutō as the first Japanese ambassador and expressing his gratitude for Japan's sympathy. Current Commentary

The Westward Retreat of Feng Zhanhai's Troops

According to yesterday's report, Feng Zhanhai's Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army has been fighting the Japanese invaders for years, traversing thousands of miles. Exhausted of ammunition and without reinforcements, he was forced to lead his troops westward. On the day of crossing the river, the soldiers, knowing that they could not take their families with them and fearing that they would be humiliated by the enemy, mostly slit the throats of their beloved wives and children before tearfully heading west. Passing through the desolate areas of western Liaoning, and at a time when nine out of ten houses were empty, they marched hurriedly, often going days without a full meal. This report is truly written with every word soaked in blood and tears, making it unbearable to finish reading. Alas, can there be anything more tragic and agonizing in this world? Since the sudden invasion by the strong enemy in the three northeastern provinces of our country, and after the complete retreat of the army responsible for defending the country and protecting its territory, the only force supporting the precarious situation and preserving our national spirit from extinction has been our Volunteer Army, lacking both supplies and weapons. With their bare hands, they fought in the frozen wilderness, causing the enemy to be discouraged and the rebels to change their colors. People all over the world have been impressed. Their loyalty, courage, bravery, and extraordinary perseverance are truly enough to move heaven and earth and cause the gods to weep. However, after fighting bitterly for so long, even though more than a year has passed, our Volunteer Army has ultimately suffered due to the lack of sustained support and the relentless increase in enemy firepower. Ma Zhanshan and Su Bingwen have already suffered defeats one after another, retreating to corners. Now, even Feng Zhanhai's troops cannot avoid retreating westward due to the exhaustion of ammunition and lack of reinforcements. Alas, while one corner is fighting desperately, the entire nation sits idly by, watching as if it were a matter of no concern. Whose fault is it that the Volunteer Army has been defeated? The closing declaration of the Third Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee stated: "The responsibility of this Party is to seek freedom and equality for China, to consolidate the integrity of the nation's territory, sovereignty, and administration. If there is any infringement upon these, we vow to resist and restore them with all our strength, together with the people of the country." This kind of announcement is resolute and deeply admired by the people of the whole country. Since the loss of the eastern provinces of our country, more than a year has passed. We have always hoped that the government would prepare to recover the lost territory, but we also feared that this hope would not easily materialize. Now, at a time when the people's morale is about to decline, the government suddenly makes this kind of announcement, which is truly enough to invigorate our people. I believe that the most urgent task for defending against disaster today is, firstly, to provide practical assistance to the Volunteer Army fighting arduously in the Northeast, so that loyal and courageous citizens will not simply look up to the sky and shed blood, lamenting the impossibility of saving the country, and that those who rise up later will be emboldened and inspired to fight for themselves. This one thing alone is enough to uphold justice in the world. What is even more heartrending is that the Volunteer Army has been fighting bitterly outside the customs for years, risking their lives in the frozen wilderness, while the people in the country enjoy themselves as usual. On the day Feng's troops slit the throats of their beloved wives and children and tearfully headed west, it was the very moment when the sons and daughters of wealthy families in the cities were reveling in wine and song in brightly lit places. Before the country has perished, the hearts of the people have already died. Like birds nesting on a hanging curtain, they are unaware of the danger. Comparing these two situations, we can only cry out to heaven in anguish. Fellow countrymen, if you still hope that our nation can be saved and that our Republic of China will not be trampled by the enemy's iron hooves, then from this day on, we must exert the strength of our entire nation to fully support the Volunteer Army, so that the enemy cannot sit securely in the three northeastern provinces. We must know that the military force that defends our nation today is actually the Volunteer Army, a military force of the people. Saving the Volunteer Army is saving the nation, and it is also saving ourselves. Fellow countrymen, awaken quickly!

The Third Plenary Session Cables Geneva to Comfort Yan, Gu, and Guo, Three Representatives

Also Sends Cables to Comfort Wang, Hu, and Central Committee Members Who Did Not Attend

(Nanjing) At the Fifth Plenary Session of the Third Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee, it was resolved to comfort the representatives of our country attending the League of Nations and to express condolences to Comrades Wang and Hu, as well as the Central Committee members who were unable to attend due to official duties or illness. The Central Secretariat issued the following four cables on the 22nd in accordance with the resolution:

(1) Cable to Representatives to the League of Nations: To Representative Yan Junren, Representative Gu Shaochuan, and Representative Guo Fuchu at the Office of the Chinese Delegation in Geneva: The representatives attended the League of Nations meeting, exerting themselves in diplomatic circles to fight for the dignity of the country and to maintain peace in the world. Your efforts and struggles have been arduous and deeply appreciated. This meeting remembers your loyalty and sends its deepest condolences. It is hoped that you will continue your efforts to complete the task. This is our earnest expectation. The Third Plenary Session of the Fourth Central Executive Committee of the Kuomintang of China.

(2) Cable to Committee Member Wang: To Comrade Wang Jingwei, via the Chinese Minister to Berlin: The plenary session has been in session for a week. Thanks to the solidarity of all comrades, major issues such as defending against foreign aggression and promoting constitutional government have been discussed and decided upon. The comrades are far away, and your old illness has not been cured. All members of the meeting are deeply concerned. Yesterday, it was unanimously decided to extend our sincere condolences. We hope that you will take care of yourself for the sake of the country, recover soon, and jointly support the great cause of the rejuvenation of the Chinese nation. The Third Plenary Session of the Fourth Central Executive Committee.

(3) Cable to Committee Member Hu: To Comrade Hu Hanmin in Hong Kong (The text of the cable is the same as the one to Comrade Wang Jingwei).

(4) Cable to Central Committee Members Who Could Not Attend the Plenary Session: To Committee Member Jiang Zuobao, Committee Member Kong Xiangxi, Committee Member Feng Yuxiang, Committee Member Li Jishen, Committee Member Shao Lizi, Committee Member Zhao Zaiwen, Committee Member Yan Xishan, Committee Member Zheng Zhanan, Committee Member Li Zonghuang, Committee Member Zhu Shaoliang, Committee Member Chen Jitang, Committee Member Zou Lu, Committee Member Deng Zeru, Committee Member Li Zongren, Committee Member Liu Luyin, Committee Member Lin Yunhai, Committee Member Lin Zhimian, Committee Member Bai Chongxi, Committee Member Yu Hanmou, Committee Member Xiang Hanping, Committee Member Liu Jiwen, Committee Member Lin Yizhong, Committee Member Miao Peinan, Committee Member Ou Fangpu, Committee Member Chen Yaoyuan, Committee Member Zhan Jushi, Committee Member Zhu Jiqing, Committee Member Lu Dipin, Committee Member Li Liejun, Committee Member He Shizhen, Committee Member Xiong Kewu, Committee Member Chen Jiayou, and all other absent Central Executive and Supervisory Committee Members: Since the opening of the Third Plenary Session, we have received telegrams from comrades requesting leave and attaching various opinions on unifying resistance against aggression and reorganizing the army for national recovery. These have been submitted for discussion, and the agenda has been focused on two points: unity in rescuing the nation from disaster and establishing a constitutional foundation. Important resolutions have been immediately announced to the whole country and are expected to be reviewed. Some comrades have been unable to attend the meeting in Nanjing due to busy schedules, responsibilities, or illness. The meeting deeply remembers the contributions of the comrades and their great concern for this meeting. We extend our condolences. The Third Plenary Session of the Fourth Central Executive Committee. (Central News Agency, 23rd)

Zhu Jiahua Cables Shanghai Describing Advantages and Disadvantages of Separation of Postal Savings

The Key to Consolidating Postal Services:

Lies in the Improvement of the Postal Industry Itself

(Nanjing) Regarding the merger of the Savings and Remittance Bureau, Zhu Jiahua sent a letter through Wu Tiecheng to the members of the Postal Economic System Research Association, stating the advantages and disadvantages of the separation and merger of postal services and savings and remittances. The main point is that the key to consolidating the postal foundation is not in the separation and merger of postal services and savings and remittances, but in the improvement of the industry itself. What needs to be paid attention to is how to ensure the safety of savings, use them wisely, and seek the interests of depositors, and how to develop the savings and remittance business, so as to promote financial circulation and increase people's savings. The postal savings and remittance industry is also a national transportation undertaking. The profit and loss of savings and remittances are the profit and loss of transportation. For related undertakings that belong to the same entity, if disputes over separation and merger affect savings and credit, it is not the original intention of those who love postal services and savings and remittances. (Special Telegram, 23rd)

Roosevelt Rejects Hoover's Offer to Jointly Resolve War Debts

To Avoid Restrictions on Post-Inauguration Administration

Official Publication of Correspondence

French Press Praises Roosevelt's Understanding of Principles

Hoover to Abandon Proposal for Forming a Committee

National News Agency, Washington, 21st – The war debt issue is now entirely left to the Democratic government to handle. Today, the American President has declared that cooperative action between him and President-elect Roosevelt has ended. Roosevelt believes it is inconvenient to agree to his proposal, and he will respect Roosevelt's wishes. A senior government official also stated that the President will no longer pursue the war debt issue during his remaining term. After making this statement, the US government immediately released the exchange of telegrams between the two Presidents. Initially, on the 17th, Hoover telegraphed Roosevelt, outlining his plan to select a bipartisan committee and asking if Roosevelt would like to join in selecting this committee, or if he preferred to postpone the entire war debt issue until after March 4th. Upon receiving the telegram, Roosevelt immediately consulted with key members of his party. It is reported that Democratic leaders believe this plan is a Republican attempt to trick the Democrats into accepting a Republican plan and a Republican committee to resolve the war debts. Therefore, on the 19th, Roosevelt replied, "I believe you will also recognize that it would be unwise for me to accept an apparent joint responsibility at a time when I have no constitutional authority to participate fully." The next day, Hoover again telegraphed Roosevelt, urging him to cooperate and requesting that he appoint Young, House, or other Democrats to consult with government officials to find a way to avoid delays. According to the Republicans, this proposal was intended to invite a Democratic representative to informally assist the cabinet in deciding on the selection of the committee and the steps to be taken. The White House anticipated that this proposal would be accepted by the Democrats, hence the optimistic tone yesterday. Unexpectedly, in the evening, they received Roosevelt's reply, stating, "If I accept joint responsibility, it will inevitably be interpreted by debtor and other nations as I have been tasked with carrying out predetermined policies and paths. I am deeply concerned that in future negotiations, or even in matters beyond debt, debtor nations may attempt to bind the new government to what is recommended or agreed upon by the current administration. However, I would be grateful to be kept informed of the current progress of the preparations for negotiations, and in the meantime, I am happy to freely contribute my opinions." After receiving the telegram, President Hoover knew that the war debt issue could not be resolved during his remaining term, and that the Republican plan to work with the Democrats to formulate negotiation strategies and resolutions would not succeed. Angered, he expressed his intention to not proceed. The resolution of the war debt issue is of great importance to large American bankers and industrialists. Therefore, the Democrats want to resolve it themselves after taking office, while the Republicans are unwilling to simply abandon it. The recent Congressional decision to require debtor nations to pay the installments due in December indicates that Hoover's moratorium plan has expired and terminated. The recent reluctance of the American President to seek to form another committee through normal diplomatic channels, the Congress's strong opposition to this move, and Roosevelt's repeated declarations that it should be handled through normal diplomatic channels are all for this reason.

Reuters, New York, 23rd – President Hoover, regarding Roosevelt's documents on war debts, believes that Roosevelt is unwilling to cooperate. Upon hearing this, Roosevelt expressed surprise and issued a statement saying that President Hoover is now making an implication that he believes that cooperative behavior on foreign issues should not be agreed to, which is regrettable. It is not only detrimental to our country but also to the resolution of world problems. In fact, he suggested to Hoover that Hoover could select his representatives to conduct preliminary research and show him the progress, and he also promised to discuss everything with President Hoover in the future and before March 4th.

Havas, Washington, 22nd – The correspondence between Hoover and Roosevelt has recently been released by the White House. British newspapers commented on Roosevelt's response, saying that they did not expect it to be so straightforward, but they still hope that Hoover's plan can succeed. However, it is not easy for European countries to only negotiate with Hoover's representatives. The documents between Hoover and Roosevelt did not have enough to make the French parliament change its attitude. The French press highly praised Roosevelt's understanding of matters and found it very fair.

China United Press, Tokyo, 23rd – The Seiyukai held a general assembly of its members at its headquarters at 2:00 PM today. Over 300 members from both houses of the Diet attended. Secretary-General Yamaguchi delivered the opening remarks, and President Suzuki gave an inspiring speech, saying that in this time of internal and external difficulties, at this unprecedented juncture for the nation, this Diet can be said to be the lifeline of the people and a major Diet for handling urgent matters. At that time, due to the Manchuria problem, for the sake of peace in the Far East, the struggle of the imperial representatives is deeply appreciated. It is hoped that our party will adopt an appropriate attitude at this time. Subsequently, Suzuki selected eleven people for the internal general affairs and secretariat positions. At 5:00 PM, a welcoming banquet was held at the San'entei.

(A) "Financial Countermeasures" (1) Measures to rescue the current situation: i. Providing real estate funds, ii. Establishing special financial institutions to provide funds to small and medium-sized industrial, commercial, and agricultural businesses, iii. Extending debt repayment periods and reducing interest rates, iv. Stabilizing exchange rates and preventing fluctuations, v. Reorganizing farm household debts, vi. Implementing government control of key industries. (2) Raising the market price of gold bullion purchases. (3) Unifying silkworm seed and managing silk. (4) Establishing a new silk sales organization under government control.

(B) "New Manchuria-Mongolia Policy" (1) Implementing Japan-Manchuria controlled economy (controlled means annexation): i. Revising the tariff law, ii. Rationalizing Japanese industry, iii. Designating Manchuria as a place where Japanese gold notes are commonly used, iv. Prioritizing Japanese interests and restricting the industrial policy of Manchukuo. (2) Facilities to be prepared for the development of Manchuria and Mongolia: i. Expanding and consolidating communication and transportation organizations in Manchuria and Mongolia, ii. Reorganizing the currency system and financial institutions in Manchuria and Mongolia, iii. Resolving the immigration problem. (3) Maintaining public order in Manchuria and Mongolia, with the Japanese army bearing full responsibility.

French Chamber of Deputies Confirms Confidence in Paul-Boncour Cabinet

Havas, Paris, 22nd – The new Premier Paul-Boncour announced the new Cabinet's program to the Chamber of Deputies. The first part of his declaration was seen in yesterday's newspaper. Now, the final paragraph is supplemented as follows. Regarding the issue of disarmament, Paul-Boncour said that the previous government had strived to eliminate the hesitation and procrastination in the Disarmament Conference. This kind of procrastination almost caused the conference to fail. The efforts of the previous government had considerable success. For example, Germany's return to the Disarmament Conference was an important result. However, the principle of equality of armaments is recognized in the concrete construction of international, or at least European, security. The French government is strictly guarding against anyone using this recognition to engage in the restoration of armaments, which would run counter to the purpose of the Disarmament Conference. Regarding agricultural issues, Paul-Boncour said that the government will soon ask the parliament to pass laws to protect the wheat market and pass new measures so that all agricultural products can receive more complete protection. Regarding the issue of unemployment, Paul-Boncour said that the government intends to continue the unfinished work of the former Minister of Labor. For those who are able to support themselves through work but have suffered unwarranted disasters, they will be provided with assistance. This is the principle of national solidarity and survival. As for the nationalization of production enterprises, the government should strive to do so, but on the condition of respecting individual rights and not hindering the independence, justice, and wholeness of workers granted by law. Overseas French colonies will also be asked to cooperate in order to seek economic recovery. This is the immediate goal of the new cabinet. Paul-Boncour said at the end of the presentation, "Today, we ask your Chamber for your confidence."

Havas, Paris, 22nd – After the new Premier Paul-Boncour issued the declaration, he immediately accepted the motion proposed by Deputy Yurin, that is, to raise the question of confidence. Yurin's motion is as follows: "The Chamber of Deputies has carefully listened to the Cabinet's declaration, believing that the government can follow the public will and continue to implement policies such as consolidating peace, reorganizing the economy and finances, maintaining social progress, and popularizing education." The case was immediately put to a vote. As a result of the vote, 379 people voted in favor and 166 people voted against, and it was passed.

Philippine Independence Act

Result of Negotiation Between the Two Houses

Compromised to Ten Years

Reduced Restrictions on Immigration and Trade

National News Agency, Washington, 22nd – Today, the US Senate passed the Philippine Independence Act after negotiation between the two houses. There was little debate. It has now been transferred to the House of Representatives, but it may not be able to be placed on the agenda before the holidays. The case includes the following points: (1) Independence is granted after a ten-year transition period, without the need to decide through a citizens' assembly. (2) From the sixth year onwards, the Philippines should implement gradually increasing export tariffs, with the tariff rate in accordance with regular US tariff rules, starting from 5% and up to 25%. (3) Export tariff revenue is used to repay Philippine public debt. (4) The duty-free amount of Philippine sugar exported to the United States should be limited to 800,000 tons of raw sugar per year and 50,000 tons of refined sugar per year. (5) The duty-free amount of coconut oil exported to the United States should be limited to 200,000 tons per year, and the duty-free amount of rope exported to the United States should be limited to 3,000,000 pounds per year. (6) The annual immigration quota from the Philippines to the United States is set at 50 people, but this provision will only take effect after the Philippine Legislative Assembly or Constitutional Convention accepts the Independence Act. (7) The United States retains the right to preserve naval and military bases in the Philippines. (8) Please ask the US President to negotiate a neutrality treaty to protect Philippine independence. It is expected that the US President will veto this case, but independence advocates in both houses believe that both houses can still have sufficient votes to override the President's veto.

A Record of Inspection in Yexian After the Calamity (Continued)

Ruined Wells, Collapsed Walls, a Land of Tiles and Rubble

A Century of Flourishing Essence Destroyed in a Single Conflict

(Public and Private Losses Difficult to Estimate) Since the outbreak of this military event, the losses to the entire county have been truly impossible to calculate. Initially, the Chamber of Commerce advanced 50,000 silver dollars, and the military commissariat prepared supplies, spending approximately over 100,000 silver dollars. After Liu Zhennian ordered self-sufficiency in supplies, the people's money, food, livestock, clothing, antiques, calligraphy, and paintings—everything the populace possessed—were requisitioned by the military, leaving almost nothing. A once-flourishing city that had not suffered from war for centuries was left with only an empty shell. How can one estimate the value of such losses? The buildings outside the four gates of the city were all demolished. Many houses inside the city were also damaged. Within five *li* of the city walls, beans and crops were not harvested, and wheat was not sown. The land is now barren for dozens of *li*, and there is no hope of harvest until July of next year. Other population and livestock suffered heavy casualties. Carts, oxen, and horses were all requisitioned. What is the total amount of all public and private losses? It is truly difficult to obtain an accurate statistic.

(The Towering City Walls Are About to Collapse) The Yexian city walls were known for their sturdy construction and neat alignment. This military event nearly hollowed them out entirely. The damage is divided into three layers: ㈠ The surface: Liu's army dug trenches on top of the city walls, several feet deep. ㈡ The middle: Liu's army dug tunnels in the middle of the city walls and excavated gun emplacements outward to fire cannons. ㈢ The foundations: Liu's army dug tunnels at the base of the city walls, creating passages inside and outside, bypassing the city gates. The entire circumference of the city was hollowed out, with holes only a few paces apart. The city walls, damaged in these three layers, are now in imminent danger of collapse. Repairing them will not be easy, and if heavy rains come, they are bound to collapse.

(Ancient Mansions and Wealthy Houses Are Emptied) Yexian was known for its wealth, and many officials emerged during the late Ming dynasty, reaching the pinnacle of fame and success. Ancient mansions and wealthy houses were everywhere. Antiques, calligraphy, and paintings were passed down through generations, and collections were quite rich. Since September 21, when Liu Zhennian ordered the military to requisition supplies independently, soldiers have openly requisitioned. Even ordinary people and small households were not spared. One can imagine what happened to those with even a slightly renowned name. The Lu family in Xiguan, a family of high-ranking officials for generations, possessed great wealth. One day, they were moving valuables into the city, including 130 fine fur coats and countless antiques and jade objects, worth approximately one million [silver dollars]. Suddenly, they encountered soldiers who requisitioned everything and took it away. Another family had six gold bricks hidden away, and they suffered the same fate. Moreover, these requisition teams, upon arriving at a home, took everything, regardless of its value. Items inconvenient to carry were destroyed. The porcelain and ancient bricks collected by one family were deemed worthless by the requisition team and were wantonly smashed. Fragments of broken bricks still fill several large carts. Yexian has suffered a great calamity, and the collections of most ancient mansions and wealthy houses have been exhausted. It is feared that they will now be on par with ordinary people.

(Explosions of Abandoned Bombs Occur Daily) After Liu's army retreated, many landmines and bombs were left buried underground, and they often detonated suddenly. Explosions occurred multiple times each day. Therefore, pedestrians were cautious, and no one dared to travel on less frequented roads. When the military conflict first arose, the beans in the fields had not yet been harvested. After Liu's army retreated, many farmers went to the fields to gather the remaining beans, triggering buried bombs, injuring people. Such incidents were frequently heard of. Currently, the Public Security Bureau has recruited a soldier who deserted from Liu's army, who is very familiar with the buried landmines. He is now being sent to the buried locations with laborers to search and dig them up. If they encounter something dangerous that they dare not move, they set fire to it from a distance to detonate it, to prevent people and livestock from accidentally triggering them and getting injured. There are also unexploded mortar shells hidden in various places, and they are also being thoroughly searched for.

(The Ninth Middle School Is Riddled with Underground Tunnels) The Ninth Middle School on Chayuan Street has spacious grounds and a large scale. Liu's army headquarters, and Liu Zhennian himself, were stationed there. More than fifty underground tunnels of various sizes were constructed. Liu himself lived in an underground tunnel in the main auditorium, dug more than ten feet into the ground. It was covered with loose soil, also about ten feet high. The soil was covered with steel plates, making it extremely sturdy. The interior was lined with mats, and the furniture and equipment were complete. Liu lived there, rarely venturing out. Other radio and command centers were also set up in the school. The school authorities are now gradually filling in the underground tunnels, actively preparing for the resumption of classes. However, most of the school equipment has been damaged, and supplementing it will be a significant undertaking.

(Careless Handling of Military Supplies Leads to Civilian Disasters) When Liu's army was about to retreat, landmines and bombs collected from various locations were stored in the Black Tiger Temple inside the West Gate. Unexpectedly, due to a moment of carelessness, a thunderous explosion occurred, destroying the entire temple. Hundreds of civilian homes in the surrounding area were also affected. Half of the nearby city wall collapsed. Two giant bells inside the temple were shattered into dozens of pieces. More than ten engineers were all killed in the explosion, leaving only severed limbs and remains. It was a tragic event.

(Eight Thousand Starving Refugees Await Relief) After Liu's army completely withdrew, people who had fled to various places gradually returned to Yexian. Upon seeing their former homes, even those that had not been reduced to rubble were left with bare walls and nothing inside. Even formerly wealthy households had nothing to live on upon their return. Widespread misery prevailed, and people cried out for food. According to a survey by the Red Swastika Society, there are more than 2,000 refugee households, totaling more than 8,000 people, urgently awaiting relief. Fortunately, the Red Swastika Societies in Qingdao, Jinan, Yantai, Longkou, and other places have come to Yexian to provide emergency relief, establishing five porridge kitchens, distributing porridge twice a day, and distributing more than 2,000 sets of cotton clothing. They are also raising 12,000 silver dollars, intending to provide relief based on the severity of the disaster, from two to twenty dollars per household. Three thousand dollars have already been distributed on the 18th. It is reported that the Qingdao Chamber of Commerce has also donated more than 500 sets of cotton clothing and is raising funds to come to Yexian for relief in the coming days.

(Organizing a Relief Committee to Handle Post-Disaster Affairs) County Magistrate Zhao Hongze, Public Security Bureau Chief Wang Weixiang, and others, recognizing the severity of the disaster and the fact that the people have no clothing or food, and that, although the Red Swastika Society and others have established porridge kitchens in Yexian, the Society's financial constraints make it difficult to sustain operations for long, and that the closure of the porridge kitchens would leave 8,000 refugees facing starvation, have jointly organized a relief committee with various government agencies and local figures to raise funds for relief. Zhao was publicly elected as the chairman, and the heads of various bureaus and the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce were elected as members. A general meeting has been held to establish six groups: investigation, distribution, fundraising, documentation, accounting, and general affairs, to actively carry out post-disaster management. (December 20)

The Guangdong Army Captures Zixi and Lichuan in Eastern Jiangxi

The Puppet Military Conference Decides on a New Plan

Zhu De and Mao Zedong Flee Southeast from the Jiangxi-Fujian Border

A dispatch from Nanchang: After the collapse of the four bandit groups of Zhu De, Mao Zedong, Peng Dehuai, and Luo Ronghuan at Xuwan, they retreated towards the Fujian border. The puppet First and Second Army Corps retreated from Xiaoshi in Nancheng to Lichuan. The puppet Fifth Army Corps retreated to Kangdu, at the junction of Nanfeng, Lichuan, and Jianning. The puppet Fourth Army was stationed in Zixi. The puppet Twenty-second Army, led by Luo Binghui, scurried around the border areas of Zixi, Guixi, and Guangze, attempting to unite with the two bandit groups led by Fang Zhimin and Shao Shiping on the Jiangxi-Zhejiang-Fujian border. However, the bandit leaders Zhu De, Mao Zedong, and Peng Dehuai, suffering significant losses in this northward invasion, convened a puppet military conference in Lichuan to salvage the remnants and reorganize. They consolidated all the remaining forces into three army corps and five military regions: (A) The puppet army corps commanders were: 1. Lin Biao, 2. Peng Dehuai, 3. Luo Binghui, and, according to one account, Dong Zhentang. (B) Ruijin and Ningdu were designated as the puppet central region, garrisoned by the puppet guard and student army. Xunwu, Anyuan, and Huichang were designated as the Jiangxi-Guangdong border region, commanded by the puppet Twentieth Army Commander Chen Yi. Chongyi, Shangyou, and Yongxin, up to Ninggang, were designated as the Jiangxi-Hunan region, commanded by the puppet Eighth Army Commander Li Tianzhu. The puppet Sixteenth Army Commander Kong Hechong was appointed as the puppet commander of the Jiangxi-Hubei-Hunan military region. The puppet Seventh and Ninth Divisions fled to eastern Hubei. The puppet Independent Division and Red Second Division hid in the mountains around Xiushui, Tongcheng, Liuyang, Wan'an, and Chongyang. The puppet Tenth Army Commander Fang Zhimin was the commander of the Jiangxi-Northeast military region. The original 82nd, 83rd, and 84th Regiments and the Red Guard Division scattered around Zhoufang, Fangdun, and Hengfeng. The puppet Twenty-second Army Commander Luo Binghui also served as the commander of the Northwest Fujian military region, with the puppet Independent 36th, 32nd, and 34th Divisions, formed by local bandits, garrisoning the border areas of Changting, Jianning, Ninghua, Guangze, and Shaowu bordering Jiangxi, and maintaining contact with the puppet Fifth Army Corps, holding on to their old nests. This is the bandits' new plan and the approximate outline of their new distribution. Earlier, the main forces of Zhu De, Mao Zedong, Peng Dehuai, and Lin Biao suffered almost complete losses in the battles of Yihuang, Jinxi, and Linchuan. Therefore, in Lichuan, Zixi, Guangze, and other areas, the puppet village soviets were forced to capture every able-bodied man to serve in the Red Army. The residents fled en masse. As for kidnapping for ransom, robbing livestock and property, these were considered secondary. On the Nationalist side, Chen Cheng, the commander of the front line on the Fu River, declared the first phase of the military campaign in eastern Jiangxi complete with the capture of Jinxi. He then came to the provincial capital with Sun Lianzhong to request instructions for the second phase of the campaign from the headquarters of the three provinces. The chief of staff, He Guoguang, discussed the plan to advance towards the Fujian border with Chen and Sun. After Chen returned to Fuzhou, he commanded the Fourth, Eighteenth, Twenty-seventh, and Thirty-seventh Armies of eastern Jiangxi to attack Zhu De and Mao Zedong in Lichuan and Zixi. A telegram from Nancheng reports that in this attack on Lichuan, the division of Zhou Zhirou served on the right wing, the division of Wu Qiwu in the center, and the division of Li Yunjie on the left wing, taking a three-sided encirclement of Lichuan from the area of Xiaoshi. After the general attack on the 19th, the bandits dared not engage and retreated towards Guangze, Shaowu, Jianning, and Guangchang. The Nationalist army completely recovered Zixi that afternoon, capturing many prisoners and pursuing the fleeing bandits southeastward. Furthermore, a dispatch from Jinxi reports that the Fifth Division, after the capture of Jinxi, largely returned to Guixi, with a portion remaining in the county town for post-war management. Its Independent Third Regiment was ordered to depart for Zixi, advancing along the way, encountering only minor resistance from scattered bandits. The regiment recovered Zixi County on the 15th and is currently managing the aftermath. Now that Zixi and Lichuan have been captured, only Guangchang Peak in eastern Jiangxi remains in the hands of the bandits. The Zhejiang-Fujian border area is now less empty than before, as Liu Zhennian's troops arrived in Pucheng and Chongan early, so the division of Zhao Guantao on the Jiangxi-Zhejiang-Fujian border is advancing towards Yihuang, attacking Fang Zhimin and Shao Shiping. Commander Zhao has left Shangrao for the front line to supervise the troops. It is believed that Fang Zhimin and Shao Shiping have lost contact with Zhu De and Mao Zedong, making it easy to defeat them in one fell swoop. (December 21)

The Founding of the Tianjin Volunteer Army Support Association

Wang Renwen and Others Elected as Directors

A dispatch from Tianjin: The Northeast Volunteer Army has risen up one after another, fighting fiercely against the enemy's cannons and firearms, exhausting the Japanese army. This heroic spirit, fighting for national dignity, is both laudable and moving. However, whether the Volunteer Army can sustain its operations depends entirely on the availability of supplies. People from all walks of life in Tianjin, aware of this, have organized the Tianjin Northeast Volunteer Army Support Association. The inaugural meeting was held at 10:00 AM on the 18th of this month at the Li Family Garden on No. 14 Road in the British Concession. The proceedings of the meeting were as follows: ㈠ Zhou Yufu was publicly elected as the temporary chairman and reported the purpose of the meeting, stating that since the fall of the Northeast, the Volunteer Army has been facing extreme difficulties in military supplies since the beginning of the resistance against Japan. People across the country have recognized this, and Northeast Volunteer Army Support Associations have been organized in Shanghai, Guangdong, and other places. However, it is also necessary for Tianjin, which is close to the Northeast and is an important town in North China, to organize. Therefore, we have established this association out of conscience and patriotism to continuously supply the Volunteer Army, so that it can resist for a long time, to recover the lost territory. ㈡ The declaration, organizational guidelines, regulations for the supervisory committee, custodian committee, and other matters were approved. ㈢ Thirty-three people, including Wang Renwen, Tang Xiangming, Yang Shounan, Bo Yizhong, Zhou Yufu, Wang Jiexia, Luo Longji, Tan Tinghui, Bian Baimei, Liu Bozhao, Qiu Changwei, Wang Qingguang, Wang Yanchu, Gui Binyu, Wang Yanling, and Yu Weihua, were elected as directors. The atmosphere at the meeting was very enthusiastic and tense. ㈥ After the meeting, the elected directors held a board meeting and immediately elected eleven standing directors, including Wang Renwen, Tang Xiangming, Yang Shounan, Zhou Yufu, Wang Jiexia, Luo Longji, Bian Baimei, Wang Qingguang, Wang Yanchu, Gui Binyu, and Wang Yanling. Gui Binyu was appointed as the director of the general affairs group, Wang Yanchu as the director of the public relations group, Wang Qingguang as the director of the investigation group, and Wang Yanling as the director of the propaganda group. At the same time, the board of directors also hired thirty-three people, including Zhang Fengge, Lin Kecheng, Lai Guogao, Zhu Longzhang, Yu Weihua, Chen Jingguo, Niu Xianjuan, Chen Jun, Niu Xianzheng, and Xu Tiancong, as fundraising committee members. It is also reported that the four groups have held joint meetings, making detailed plans and actively carrying out their respective tasks.

Guangdong Province Actively Implements Winter Defense

The North River Training Division Recalled to the Provincial Capital

Municipal Land and Water Police Intensify Security

A dispatch from Guangzhou: Recently, as the end of the old and new lunar years approaches, stores are busy with year-end accounts and frequent transactions of funds. As a matter of routine, the authorities conduct winter defense during this period. It is reported that the military authorities, to protect the provincial capital, have ordered the entire Training Division currently stationed in the North River to return to defend Guangzhou, stationing them at key locations in the suburbs to prevent theft by petty criminals. Within the city of Guangzhou, the Provincial Public Security Bureau began implementing winter defense on the 20th of this month. All armed security teams of the Public Security Bureau have temporarily suspended training and have been organized into armed patrol teams, patrolling the main thoroughfares near their original locations. The detective section of the Public Security Bureau has also been ordered to dispatch plainclothes detectives to various public security sub-bureaus starting on the 20th, to assist the sub-bureaus in winter defense. All off-duty police officers from the sub-bureaus will form patrol teams each day, patrolling the city day and night. During the day, detectives will go to various docks, stations, and entertainment venues to investigate criminals. At night, sub-bureau officers will lead armed police to search restaurants, hotels, inns, theaters, opium dens, and gambling houses, paying attention to the presence of petty criminals. During the period of heightened security, special attention will be paid to any changes in household registrations. Officers are not allowed to leave their posts without special cause. On the Pearl River, the Water Police Sub-Bureau will deploy additional armed water police to assist patrol ships in closely inspecting passing vessels in the main waterways. All rural ferries and foreign steamers docking must undergo inspection of disembarking passengers. As for the brothel boats and pleasure boats, which are usually mixed with the good and bad, they are confined to a fixed location and are not allowed to approach other vessels. Small boats that take in lodgers are prohibited from accommodating guests at night. (December 16)

Shandong Provincial Library's Rich Collection

A dispatch from Jinan: Wang Xiantang, the director of the Provincial Library, has spared no effort in collecting antiquities in recent years. The library already has a Han Dynasty Relief Hall and a Luo Quan Building. Now, there are plans to build a Shang Pottery Room to specially house the Qin and Han bricks and tiles of Gao Hansheng of Weixian, as well as the finest examples of Six Dynasties Buddhist statues. More than thirty stone statues have already been collected, and the gilded relief stone statues are rare treasures. Recently, another ten statues have been purchased. One is a Qingtai Second Year (Tang Dynasty) tomb epitaph made of brick by Yan Sheng. The other nine stones are all Qi Dynasty statues unearthed at the border between Guangrao and Linzi. Because there was a Thousand Buddha Temple in that area during the Six Dynasties, which was destroyed long ago, there were many statues in the temple. Several stones had already been discovered and taken away. These statues have all been transported to the library. They include: ㈠ Qingtai Second Year (Tang Dynasty) brick tomb epitaph of Yan Sheng (unearthed in Qingzhou) ㈡ Le'an Zhu Hai statue from the Tenth Year of Tianbao (Qi Dynasty) ㈢ Sun Moning statue (Qi Dynasty) ㈣ Statue from Binshan et al. from the Tiantong period (Qi Dynasty) ㈤ Li Pan brothers statue from the Second Year of Wuping (Qi Dynasty) ㈥ Shi Yingshi statue from the Fourth Year of Heqing (Qi Dynasty) ㈦ Fan Zhen statue from Yangxin from the Fourth Year of Tianbao (Qi Dynasty) ㈧ Shao Chouzhu statue from the Tenth Year of Tianbao (Qi Dynasty) ㈨ Zhang Zhan statue from Le'an from the Heqing period (Qi Dynasty) ㈩ Zhang Zuohu statue from Le'an from the Fifth Year of Tiantong (Qi Dynasty) (The above are all relics of the Thousand Buddha Temple.)

Bombing Incident Occurs in Wuhu

The Bombed Were One Silk Store and Two Cloth Stores

The Bomb Throwing Youths Identified Themselves as an Anti-Traitor Group

A dispatch from Wuhu: At about 5:00 PM today, the Xi Jinglun Silk Store in Changjie Doumen Lane and the Hengfengxiang and Heji cloth stores (located in the same place) near the Sansheng Archway in this port were simultaneously bombed by people identifying themselves as the "Save-the-Nation Dare-to-Die Comrades Association Anti-Traitor Group Dare-to-Die Team on the Anti-Japanese Front Anti-Traitor Group". Three youths went to the stores together, mostly dressed in Western style. They entered the stores under the pretense of visiting, then threw bombs and left immediately. Although the bomb at Xi Jinglun did not explode, all the store staff were panicked. They immediately reported to the police station, who took away the abandoned bomb. The bomb at Heji landed next to the Hengfengxiang counter, outside the goods cabinet. It exploded with a loud bang, filling the air with smoke. The daughter (16 years old) of the manager of that store, Bei Zuoqing, was coming out from inside, and the pupil of her left eye was shattered by the explosion. She was immediately sent to Zhong Shouzhi Hospital for treatment. The floor was blown into a large hole, and the glass cabinets and goods were also damaged. The neighboring stores, startled by this incident, closed their doors one after another, closing shop early. Afterwards, the military and police authorities were notified and dispatched teams to the scene, but it was impossible to catch the perpetrators. Soon after, the cloth stores all received a warning letter from the anti-traitor group, stating that they must seal up all enemy goods within a certain number of days and declare this in the newspapers, or else they would be bombed without mercy. It is reported that Xi Jinglun Silk Store had previously had a dispute with the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association for selling Japanese goods. (December 21)

Reasons for Jiangsu Provincial Government's Announcement of Abolishing the Industry Department

After the Jiangsu Provincial Government abolished the Department of Industry, some local people opposed it. Yesterday, the Provincial Government specially issued an order to the county governments, explaining in detail the reasons for abolishing the Department of Industry, in the hope that the local people could understand. The following is an excerpt from the order: "Upon investigation, most provinces have not established an Industry Department. Even Zhejiang Province and Jiangsu Province, which are among the best defended, as well as provinces wealthier than Jiangxi and Zhejiang, still lack such departments. Although Hubei once established a Department of Agriculture and Mines, it was subsequently abolished. This shows that the financial capacity of the Chinese government, the level of development of agriculture, industry, commerce, and mining, and the state of the national economy have not yet reached the stage where a dedicated department can be established. Since the reorganization of the Agriculture and Mines Department into the Industry Department in Jiangsu Province, the various agricultural, industrial, commercial, and mining sectors have not seen significant results, while the annual expenditure of the department and its affiliated agencies has exceeded one million. At a time when the treasury is empty and all important government affairs are feeling the pinch, spending huge sums of money annually, mostly on industrial administration and promotional expenses, is not practically effective. Judging from the principles of economics, this is unwise. If we look at the provinces in the country that have not established an Industry Department, their industrial development is no less advanced than that of Jiangsu. Moreover, since Jiangsu Province had the Department of Agriculture and Mines and later changed to the Industry Department, has its industrial performance in the past few years been superior to that of other provinces? In general, there are priorities and urgencies, and in an era of financial hardship, one should naturally prioritize what is important and urgent, so as not to hinder each other and lead to stagnation. There are countless important government affairs to be handled in this province, and for the past year, many have been difficult to promote due to limited funding. This government, learning from the past, cannot but shift from gradual to urgent measures to seek a fundamental solution. After repeated discussions and careful consideration by this government's committee, it was unanimously agreed that there is no need to establish a Department of Industry given the current financial situation and the level of industrial and commercial development in this province. Moreover, according to Articles 8, Section 2 and Section 3 of the revised provincial government organization law, the committee of this government decided to temporarily abolish the Department of Industry and merge the relevant departments under its jurisdiction into the Department of Construction for concurrent management, in order to reduce expenditures. This is permissible under the law and in accordance with the facts. In the future, when the financial resources and material strength of this province and the development of industry have reached a considerable level, and there is a need to establish a dedicated management agency, it will be easy to establish. Furthermore, although the department is temporarily abolished, efforts will still be made to improve industrial undertakings and prevent them from being suspended. It is only out of a sense of the current provincial treasury's extreme shortage, the depletion of material resources, and the people's suffering under the heavy burden that the expenditures of the institutions are seen as worthless. Therefore, we must seek the most economical methods for effective improvement, considering all aspects with painstaking effort. In fact, the current industrial administration spends such huge sums of money annually, focusing on formalities and ostentation. What the people need is not an empty organizational name, but practical undertakings. This abolition of the department will not only not hinder industrial undertakings but will also fundamentally reorganize and further develop them. Therefore, this government has decided that all affiliated institutions of the department should be temporarily closed by the end of the year, and other methods of unified reorganization will be ordered separately. The original venues, funds, and public property should be taken over and managed separately by the department and the counties, without any loss, and reports should be made. The reason is that the previous state of industrial administration had too many institutions, and the expenditures were too vast, with too much being spent on administrative expenses each year and too little being used for undertakings. At the same time, there was a lack of coordination with vocational education and agricultural education, so that specialized talents could not be increased and scientific knowledge could not be advanced. Future planning must correct the previous drawbacks. Regarding expenses, we must strive to reduce them, save all administrative expenses, and transfer them to the needs of undertakings. Regarding education, we must pay attention to vocational and rural education, encouraging learning and nurturing talent, so as to connect them. Regarding undertakings, we must concentrate the province's manpower and talent to study one by one all matters related to agriculture, sericulture, cotton spinning, animal husbandry, forestry, as well as industry, commerce, and mining, in order to achieve practical results and improve them. At the same time, regarding seeds, fertilizers, pest control, disaster preparedness, and other issues related to industry, we will select those that have been proven effective in the country and order the counties to supervise the people to implement and promote them, so as to induce improvement. In short, we will seek full development with limited resources. Although the agency is abolished, the undertakings still exist. Although expenses are saved, efforts are still made to expand them in practice. We will use the most economical and effective methods to solve the practical industrial problems needed by the society and the people, and we will never allow the government's limited money to be wasted on useless things, nor will we allow the undertakings needed by the people to be stagnated. This is the determination of this government to abolish the Department of Industry, and it is the true meaning of what is called separate unified planning. Abolishing the agency is a comprehensive plan in terms of finance, and improving industry is a necessary measure in terms of politics. The two do not hinder each other and can be carried out in parallel without contradiction. If one believes that abolishing the agency means stopping the undertakings, and if malicious people make far-fetched interpretations, it may be for ulterior motives. Those with knowledge of the matter, weighing the pros and cons in light of the facts, will understand without needing to argue. In addition to ordering the Department of Construction to carefully plan and improve the measures and to submit reports separately, we hereby order the county to immediately inform, and must follow the above instructions and earnestly implement them, and not make any misinterpretations, so as to avoid causing mistakes."

Suzhou

Nine County Joint Defense Meeting Minutes

The seventh meeting of the Wu, Kun, Qing, Jiang, Song, Jin, Xi, Wu, and Yi nine-county joint defense was held yesterday (the 23rd) at the Wu County Government. Attendees included: Songjiang County Magistrate Shen, Qingpu County Magistrate Yu Ding, Jinshan County Magistrate Tu Kaiyu, Yixing County Magistrate Sun Gongqi, Wuxi County Magistrate Chen Chuande, Wujiang County Magistrate Wang Zhengcheng, Wujin County Magistrate Zhang Pengzhu, Kunshan County Magistrate Cheng Ruji, Wu County Magistrate Zou Jing, Wu County Police Captain Du Hongyi, the 23rd District Chief of the Provincial Water Police Force Shen Weiying, Bandit Suppression Headquarters Inspector Su Shufan, Wu County Government First Section Chief Wang Pei, and Wu County Public Security Bureau Chief Inspector Zhang Nancun, totaling fourteen people. (2) Affix the license to the rear center of the boat. Wuxi

Silk Sales Prosperous

Since the autumn silkworm season began this year, the silk market has once again trended downwards, with prices dropping to 500 taels upon entering the customs. This is primarily due to the sharp decline in overseas Japanese silk prices, leaving Chinese silk with virtually no buyers. Domestic silk factories, seeing the silk market continuously declining, have also largely adopted a wait-and-see approach, refraining from purchasing. In recent days, American and French firms, due to short-selling futures, have been actively covering their positions, causing a sudden turnaround in the silk market and a surge in prices. Currently, Zhuang's 83-point Ivenna silk can be sold for 620 taels, and 80-point silk can be sold for 570-580 taels. French firms, such as the Double Eagle brand from the Zhenyi Silk Factory in this county, can sell for 650 taels. New-style, machine-made, re-reeled 13-15 thread silk can be sold for 690 taels. Domestic general silk factories are also actively purchasing. Currently, ordinary household silk is priced at 540-550 taels, while higher-quality goods require 580-590 taels. The price of dried cocoons has now risen to over 180 yuan. Based on a silk extraction ratio of 470-480 jin, the cost of cocoons per dan of silk is over 600 taels. Recently, the sales of silk from various factories in this county have been exceptionally brisk.

Major Fire Kills Two Boys

The home of Lü Mei, located in Houcun, Xixixiang Village, near Meicun in the Tenth District, caught fire the night before due to a cooking fire that ignited a pile of firewood. In an instant, the fierce flames rose and were unstoppable, spreading to neighboring houses. Lü's wife, awakened from a dream, immediately grabbed her two-year-old granddaughter and escaped naked. She attempted to rush back in to rescue her two sons, but the house had already collapsed, and the flames engulfed her, causing burns all over her body. The outer layers of her head and face peeled off, and fresh blood flowed. Her two sons, aged nine and four, were buried in the inferno. By the time the fire brigade arrived, over forty houses in the entire alley had been reduced to ashes, resulting in significant losses. Furthermore, the firewood shed belonging to residents Zhu Meisheng and Zhu Shouchang in Daxu Alley, Fourth District, also caught fire the night before, spreading to the homes of Zou Ju, Zhu Xiangsheng, and Zhu Huanqing. Over twenty houses were burned down, along with four pigs and sheep. Also, the firewood shed of Guo Guansheng's family on Baxi Bridge West Street was also carelessly ignited yesterday afternoon. Fortunately, it was daytime, and fire brigades from various locations rushed to the scene to extinguish the flames, which were quickly put out. As a result, two houses were burned down.

Jiangyin

Fortunately, none of them were in mortal danger.

Qingjiang

Cake Shop Strike Resolved

The strike by various dim sum shops in Huaiyin over business taxes has lasted for four days. On the 17th, the workers paraded in formation, with workers from Yangzhuang and Matou participating, making the situation serious. County Magistrate He, believing that during this time of heightened winter defense, unscrupulous individuals might take advantage of the situation, and fearing unexpected events that could affect public order, immediately sent a letter to Colonel Liu Zhongqi of the 340th Regiment of the garrison army, requesting him to order his subordinates to assist the county police in maintaining order. After receiving the letter, Liu announced a curfew at 11 PM that night, prohibiting large groups of idlers from parading in the streets. At the same time, County Magistrate He also ordered Peng Tingjie, the captain of the political police, to summon representatives of the cake shops to the county. Under the persuasion of Liu Qixin, the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, they were instructed to resume business as soon as possible. After discussions until about 1 AM, the representatives finally agreed to pay 40 yuan in taxes for the autumn and winter seasons of this year, and 40 yuan per quarter in the 22nd year, totaling 160 yuan for the whole year. They agreed to resume business uniformly on the morning of the 18th, and the workers from Yangzhuang and Matou also completely left the city. The strike thus came to an end.

Yangzhou

Land Tax Upheaval Loss Statistics

The losses suffered by the heads and deputies of districts, townships, and towns in this county due to the land tax upheaval have been listed and reported to the county. The victims were 45 households in the 243rd district. The total loss is estimated to be over 150,000 yuan. County Magistrate Ma has already devised a method to raise funds for relief.

Gaoyou

Kidnappers Deliver Note, Rob Large Sum

The youngest son of farmer Chen Zhiying in Ping'an Township, Second District of the county, was kidnapped by bandits last month, and there has been no news of him. Unexpectedly, around 2 AM the night before, the bandits returned Chen's youngest child and then tied up Chen's entire family. The bandits rushed into the bedroom and thoroughly searched it, robbing 600 yuan in cash and then firing their guns as they left. By the time the police team from the Longbenzhen Garrison heard the sound and came to pursue them, the bandits had already escaped without a trace.

Zhao Jiahe Salt Smugglers' Armed Fight

Salt smugglers Yao Rudong and Ji Zhenglai previously jointly smuggled over one hundred dan of illicit salt in Dengjiazhao, Yancheng, and transported it to Zhao Jiahe, Youyi, for sale. However, one boat of illicit salt, totaling 25 dan, was intercepted by the anti-smuggling camp. Yao and Ji both refused to acknowledge the loss, leading to a conflict. Each gathered over one hundred apprentices and engaged in an armed fight. As a result, one person was killed and over ten were seriously injured. Ji's bandits were defeated and fled to the northeast.

Xiaoshan

Robbed and Burned

The Feng family in Dangshanwan, East Township, Xiaoshan, was suddenly attacked by over ten bandits on the night of the 19th. They broke into the house by destroying the back window and looted it, taking all the clothing and ornaments, worth over 700 silver yuan. After the bandits left, a fire accidentally started, burning down three houses and causing a loss of over 5,000 yuan.
