Sun Ke, Wu Chaoshu and Others Return to Shanghai Yesterday After the Close of the Third Plenary Session

Sun and Wu Both Say the Impression of the Plenary Session Was Very Good

Sun's Inauguration Date as President of the Legislative Yuan is Undetermined

Wu Expresses His Unwillingness to Serve as Ambassador to the United States

And Talks About the Chinese People Should Wash Away Their Dependence Mentality

The Third Plenary Session has closed, and the attending Central Committee members are leaving Beijing one after another. Those who returned to Shanghai by overnight train from Beijing at 8 AM yesterday included: Central Committee members Sun Ke, Wu Chaoshu, Zhang Huichang, Chen Ce, Chen Qingyun, Liang Hancao, Cui Guangxiu, Li Renren, Guan Suren, Zhang Dingfan, Deng Qingyang, Pan Yunchao, Li Qi'an, Xiao Jishan, Yang Hu, Qian Dajun, etc. This reporter interviewed Sun and Wu yesterday morning. They spoke about the impression of the plenary session, as well as various domestic and foreign policy issues. Sun said he agreed to become President of the Legislative Yuan. Wu said he had firmly declined the position of Minister of Judicial Administration and was also unwilling to serve as Ambassador to the United States. As for the chairmanship of the Foreign Affairs Committee and other positions, he would consider them further. The following is a detailed account:

(Sun Talks About the Impression of the Plenary Session) After getting off the train, Mr. Sun went directly to his private residence on Columbia Road. This reporter went to visit him around 10 AM yesterday morning and was granted an audience. Mr. Sun first said that his personal impression of this Third Plenary Session was very good. All parties were able to implement a spirit of sincere unity and cooperation. Therefore, the result of the Third Plenary Session is that the first point is that it can represent the consistency of opinions within the Kuomintang, focusing on saving the country from foreign invasion. The second point is that all resolutions can represent the overall opinion of the party and the ardent demands of the entire nation. It is hoped that in the future, the power of cooperation between the government and the people can promote their realization one by one. The reporter then asked about the situation in Guangdong and whether there were any special opinions. It was said that Guangdong also expressed great appreciation for the resolutions of the Plenary Session.

(Hope for Chiang's Military Commission Leadership) The reporter asked about the feelings of Chairman Chiang of the Military Commission. He replied that Mr. Chiang's attitude was extremely sincere this time, especially on the issue of constitutional preparation, hoping to promote its early realization as much as possible. At that time, there was quite a bit of criticism, but Chiang explained in detail before it ended.

(Preliminary Rules for Trying Constitutional Government) Mr. Sun also said that the National Political Council, which the Plenary Session decided to convene next year, is a central public opinion organ and a preliminary rule for trying constitutional government during the period of political tutelage. However, the highest administrative power still lies with the Central Executive Committee. It will not be until the National Assembly is convened in March of the 24th year that the constitution will be formally formulated, the civil rights government will be organized, and genuine democracy will be implemented.

(China and Russia Negotiate Treaties) China and Russia have now formally announced the resumption of diplomatic relations. As for the Sino-Russian Non-Aggression Treaty and the Treaty of Commerce, etc., they must be negotiated after the mutual dispatch of ambassadors. Mr. Yan Huiqing's appointment as envoy to Russia has been agreed to by the other party. After being approved by the Central Political Council, it can be formally announced. As for the Soviet Ambassador to China, it is said that he will be transferred from the former ambassador to Persia.

(National Defense Determined Plan) Regarding the issue of national defense, there was also a very detailed discussion in the plenary session. The Military Commission also had a detailed plan report. Definite measures have been discussed for the expansion of aviation. However, since it concerns military affairs, it is not convenient to publish it. As for the issue of naval construction, due to the excessive amount of money needed and the training of talents, it cannot be effective in a short period of time. Therefore, it can only be gradually supplemented based on the needs of coastal defense.

(Chiang Will Go to Jiangxi to Suppress Bandits) Regarding the issue of bandit suppression, the remnants of the bandits in Henan, Anhui, and Hubei, led by Xu Xiangqian and He Long, have infiltrated Shaanxi, and they will be wiped out soon. However, the Red bandits in Jiangxi are rampant. It is said that Mr. Chiang will personally go to supervise the suppression. After the military command is unified, it will be easier to eliminate them.

(Change of Provincial Government System) The Plenary Session decided to abolish the provincial government committee system and change it to a provincial governor system. The implementation of the provincial governor system can concentrate the powers of the provincial governor, and the responsibility is specialized, making it easier to handle affairs. On the other hand, a provincial council is established as a local public opinion organ to participate in the reform of provincial administration and to supervise the provincial governor to avoid slipping into personal dictatorship. The provincial council is also a transitional public opinion organ during the period of political tutelage, and the public opinion organ during the constitutional period is the provincial people's congress. The plenary session only decided on the principle of changing the provincial system. The detailed regulations will be discussed and decided by the Central Political Council.

(Decision to Become President of the Legislative Yuan) I have decided to become the President of the Legislative Yuan. The date of taking office in Beijing has not yet been determined. There have been no major changes in the heads of the various courts. The reporter asked whether Mr. Wang has recently returned to China. It was said that Mr. Wang has not yet recovered his health and needs to continue to recuperate. There is no news of his return to China for the time being.

(Wu Chaoshu Expresses His Opinion) This reporter visited Mr. Wu Chaoshu at his residence at 9 AM yesterday morning. The main points of Wu's speech are summarized as follows: (1) The results of this Third Plenary Session are extremely satisfactory. Various resolutions are the most important plans for our country at present. (2) There have been various speculations from the outside world about my future position. All parties hope that I will serve as the Chairman of the Foreign Affairs Committee, or Ambassador to the United States, or Minister of Judicial Administration. I have firmly declined the position of Minister of Judicial Administration, and I am also unwilling to serve as Ambassador to the United States. I am still considering which position to take. (3) The resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia is the path that our country's diplomacy should follow. However, if the Chinese people rely on the League of Nations, the United States, or Soviet Russia, the result will still be failure. The victory of diplomacy lies entirely in self-reliance. I hope that the Chinese people will wash away their dependence mentality, unite as one, and work hard to save themselves.

Zhenru District Cotton Crop Failure, City Government Approves Reduction of Summer Tax

Municipal Committee member of Zhenru District, Hong Lanxiang, etc., reported to the Municipal Government that the autumn cotton harvest in the district was poor and requested a reduction in taxes, etc. The Municipal Government ordered the Land, Finance, and Social Bureaus to conduct a joint survey and reply. The bureaus reported, in brief, that although the cotton crops in the district had adequate branches and leaves, the flowers and bolls were sparse and the cotton fluff was not fully developed. This was due to the severe drought during the hot season and the scarcity of rainfall. After the beginning of autumn, hurricanes and rainstorms followed one another, causing the cotton bolls to fall off. The loss was estimated to be over 50% on average. Other crops, such as soybeans and vegetables, were slightly more resistant to wind and rain than cotton, and the harvest was still good, with a maximum loss of only 10%. It was further calculated that the allocation of crop cultivation in the district this year was 50% for cotton, 30% for soybeans, 15% for vegetables, and 0.5% for others. Now, by comprehensively calculating the allocation of cultivated area and the degree of damage to various crops in the district, the total percentage of loss is 30%, which is in line with Article 6 of the city's disaster reporting and compensation measures. After consultation, the bureaus decided to include it in Grade C and proposed a general reduction of 0.05 of the summer tax to provide relief. In addition, the summer tax serial registration book for this year has already been issued by the Land Bureau and cannot be exempted. According to the provisions in the second paragraph of Article 6 of the city's disaster reporting and compensation measures, it is proposed to use it to offset the summer tax in the 22nd year, etc. After receiving the report, the Municipal Government instructed the Land and other three bureaus: "The report has been reviewed. Since the joint survey confirms that the disaster is true, permission should be granted to reduce the tax payment to show sympathy. The Land Bureau should quickly prepare a clear list of the disaster-stricken fields and the amount of tax reduction, and the Finance Bureau should verify it and add a seal before submitting it for review and transfer. This is an order."

Rice and Wheat Temporarily Allowed to Be Exported from the Province

The Shanghai County Government issued a notice yesterday: "Ordered by the Jiangsu Provincial Government, it has been found that the provincial government committee has discussed matters at its 551st meeting. The first item, proposed by the chairman, is that the province's rice and grain production in moderate years is only sufficient for self-sufficiency. Therefore, it has been prohibited from leaving the country for many years to maintain the people's food supply. This year's autumn harvest across the country has been bountiful, and the price of grain has fallen sharply. Farmers rely on the autumn harvest for their livelihood. Now that the price of grain has plummeted, the economy of farmers in this province has been greatly affected. If remedial measures are not taken quickly, the countryside will face the danger of bankruptcy. In addition to ordering the counties to earnestly handle grain storage and to conduct assessments within the prescribed time limit in accordance with previous orders, in order to increase demand, it is now proposed to temporarily allow the province's food to be exported from the province in order to raise the price of grain and alleviate the people's difficulties. Whether or not it should still be publicly decided has been discussed and resolved. For the purpose of adjusting social finance and rural economic activity, the province's rice and wheat are allowed to be sold outside the province, but a passport must be submitted to the county government for verification. Passports are not charged. If anyone transports it out of the province privately without a passport, it will still be investigated, prohibited, and punished in accordance with the regulations. In addition to notification, an order is hereby issued to the county for compliance and a public notice shall be issued to inform the public. This order is hereby issued.

Fierce Battle Between Police and Bandits on the Shanghai-Taicang Road Results in the Shooting of a Police Officer

Yesterday morning at 12:00 AM, a police officer protecting the cable of the Liu Hang Radio Station was shot and killed by bandits in front of a pavilion about six *li* north of the Dachang Station on the Shanghai-Taicang Highway. Details are as follows:

Protecting the Cable

The Liu Hang Radio Station, directly under the Ministry of Communications, had its cables (i.e., steel wires) frequently stolen in the area along the Shanghai-Taicang Road. Therefore, it specially requested the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau to assign three police officers and one sergeant from the fourth district of Zhabei to be stationed at the radio station. They patrolled the Shanghai-Taicang Road on bicycles at night to check for cable theft. It is said that they had captured cable thieves several times in the past and sent them to the Fourth District Police Bureau for interrogation and release. The thieves harbored resentment against the police officers and had ambushed them twice with gunfire, but the police officers repelled them.

Incident Details

Last night (Thursday) around 9:00 PM, Sergeant Guo Zhenqi dispatched police officers Shi Xingdong, Liu Fangqing, and Jin Changyou on patrol. When they reached the pavilion at the 56th map mark, they were ambushed with gunfire again. Since the police officers had experienced this several times before, they were not surprised. They immediately jumped off their bicycles and returned fire from the fields. The sound of gunfire was as dense as a string of pearls. The bandits, outnumbered, were also scattered by the police officers. Later, they rode to Dachang and reported the situation to the Dachang Police Bureau. At 12:00 AM, they returned to their station in Liu Hang. Unexpectedly, when passing in front of the pavilion, the bandits placed stone bars (usually used as seats) in the middle of the road. Because it was dark, the police officers did not see them. The bicycle wheels crashed into the stone bars, and the police officers fell to the ground. The bandits opened fire again. The police officers had run out of bullets in their pistols and could not fight back. Shi Xingdong was shot in the nose and died. The bandits, seeing that their goal had been achieved, fled immediately. Police officers Liu and Jin, knowing that their partner had been killed, returned to the station to report the incident. They also informed the dead officer's wife, Mrs. Lu, in Gujia Town, and reported to the Fourth District Police Bureau.

The district chief went to investigate the scene in person around 10:00 AM yesterday and confirmed the incident. He ordered the local security chief to go to the Baoshan County Government to request an autopsy.

Corpse Observation

After hearing the news yesterday, the reporter took the Shanghai-Taicang bus to observe the scene. The corpse was lying face down in a pool of blood by the side of the road, head northwest and feet southeast. One hand was outstretched, and the other was clenched. There was a felt hat in front of the head. The deceased was wearing a black wool overcoat, leggings, straight-cut cloth shoes, black velvet socks, and had a shaved head. It seemed that the bullet had not passed through, as the corpse was lying face down and there was a gun hole in the back of the head. The stone bar was still placed by the side of the road.

Conversation with the Corpse's Wife

Later, I saw a young woman in white inside the pavilion and knew that she must be a member of the deceased's family. I had the following conversation with her. The corpse's wife, Mrs. Shi Lu, said that she was 21 years old and from Jiaxing. Her parents were still alive. She married Shi Xingdong two years ago and had a daughter who had died. She is currently five months pregnant. Her deceased husband was 32 years old and from Suqian County, Jiangsu Province. His parents, brothers, and sisters are also alive. This morning (yesterday morning), after her husband was shot dead by bandits, a police officer with the surname Jin rushed to the scene. The deceased was not yet dead but could not speak. He only raised his hand to signal. According to onlookers, they heard gunshots at the time, but it was late at night and there were no villages nearby, so they dared not go out to see what happened.

Shanghai-South Public Bus Company's Exclusive Operating Rights Revoked

Due to Business Losses, Suspension of Operations, and Inability to Resume

Decision Made After Being Brought up in the Municipal Council Two or Three Times

The Shanghai-South Public Bus Company suspended operations and cleared its accounts on August 30th of this year due to business losses. The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities believed that the public bus business operated by the company was of great importance to public transportation and was of an exclusive nature, so it could not be allowed to be suspended for a long time. After reporting to the Municipal Government for approval, on October 3rd, the company was ordered to complete the clearing procedures and resume traffic before November 30th. If it failed to do so, the exclusive operating rights would be revoked. Subsequently, Mr. Jiang Wanping, the liquidator of the company, replied, stating that after checking the asset and liability status, the existing assets were clearly insufficient to cover the liabilities. According to the Company Law, it was necessary to apply for bankruptcy, and there was no possibility of continuing operations. He could only plead that when inviting tenders for another company to operate, the existing assets should be given a more favorable price or a special permit for reorganization and transfer should be granted to provide relief. The Bureau of Public Utilities believed that since the company had no possibility of continuing operations and the public transportation in Shanghai-South could not be allowed to be suspended for a long time, it requested the Municipal Government to issue an order revoking the company's exclusive operating rights, returning the deposit guarantee, and declaring the contract signed with the Municipal Government on September 18, 1928, and the supplementary contract signed on March 20, 1931, invalid. The Municipal Government submitted the report to the 223rd Municipal Council meeting, which decided that the exclusive operating rights of the Shanghai-South Public Bus Company should be revoked immediately, and the Bureau of Public Utilities should find a way to restore traffic in Shanghai-South. Yesterday, the order was issued to the Bureau of Public Utilities to comply.

Shanghai Municipal Council Considers Milk Disinfection Measures

At the last meeting of the Health Committee, the Director of the Health Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council, proposed a plan to ensure the quality of milk within the concession. According to the opinions of the veterinarians in the bureau, although various measures have been implemented to regulate Grade B milk in the concession, it is still a source of disease. Although bovine tuberculosis is not common in Shanghai, typhoid fever and dysentery may be transmitted through milk. The doctor suggested that the Shanghai Municipal Council establish a new-style disinfection plant to disinfect Grade B milk. The purchase of land, construction, and equipment for this plant would cost about 250,000 taels of silver. However, if a fee of three cents of silver is charged for each pint of milk sent for disinfection, the plant could be profitable and would not need to be funded by taxes. Therefore, Dr. Zhou Deng, Director of the Health Department, requested that this proposal or other good strategies be considered, or that private individuals could be allowed to operate this business. The Acting Director of the Finance Department expressed his deep sympathy for the benefits of disinfecting Grade B milk for hygiene. However, during this time of financial constraints, all temporary expenses should be limited to those that are absolutely necessary for municipal administration. The disinfection plant did not seem absolutely necessary, so he could not support the proposal to build a plant. Subsequently, the Chairman of the Committee stated that if this plant were established, it would seem that the Shanghai Municipal Council would be in business competition with Grade A milk factories. Although the matter is beneficial, it seemed better to allow private individuals to handle it, or that the Grade B factories could jointly operate this business. The Director of the Health Department replied that it was doubtful whether the factories had the financial resources. If the current licensing regulations were tightened, requiring Grade B milk to be disinfected, the result might be to drive the milk factories out of the concession, making them even more difficult to manage. Furthermore, if each factory disinfected itself, the price of milk would increase, which would be inconvenient for poorer users. The bureau would have to send personnel to supervise everywhere, which would be too much trouble. Then a committee member said that the supply of milk in the concession was currently in short supply. He thought that drinking and cooking milk could be divided into two categories so that the disinfection proposal could be implemented. After discussion, all committee members agreed that it was necessary to disinfect milk universally and that it was a profitable business. If the public knew the bureau's intentions, private individuals would be willing to operate this plant. For detailed consideration, a small committee of three should be appointed to review the matter and report back. All committee members should also consider this issue again so that it could be discussed again at the next meeting. The Director of the Health Department should also send the committee a copy of the nationality of the owners of each Grade B factory and the production volume of each factory for reference. This case was submitted to the Board of Directors on the 21st, and the Board of Directors approved the methods adopted.

Photography Experts Hold Tea Party to Discuss Submission Methods for the Chicago Exposition

On-the-Spot Recognition of Submissions: Very Satisfactory Results

The China Travel Service has been entrusted by the Preparatory Committee for China's Participation in the Chicago Exposition to collect photography submissions from China for display in the United States. The company believes that this matter is of great importance, so it has specially hired contemporary celebrities and photography experts to form a committee to oversee everything. The work is progressing very smoothly, and many submissions have already been collected. The company held a tea party at 4:00 PM yesterday on the eighth floor of the Hua An Building to entertain local photography experts and editors of various pictorial magazines. The details are as follows:

Attendees

The people who attended yesterday included Ye Gongchuo, Song Yunpu, Zhou Jianfu, Cao Zuguang, Wang Dafo, Teng Gu, Wang Xiaoting, Peng Wangshi, Hu Bozhou, Liu Shuofu, Li Zunyong, Huang Bodi, Chen Xiaofang, Jiang Xiaojian, Shao Yuxiang, Ma Guoliang, Zheng Wuchang, Zuo Gengsheng, Lang Jingshan, Chen Wanli (who came specially from Hangzhou), Chen Long, Huang Zhongchang, Liu Xucang, Cai Renbao, Zhu Shuren, Xu Zuyin, Daniel North, Hu Boxiang, Zhang Zhenyu, Zhang Zhenhou, Chen Chuanlin, Shao Woyun, Guo Xilin, and more than 30 other people. On behalf of the travel service, Song Chunfang, Zhang Shuiqi, Zhao Junhao, and Zhu Tongjiu welcomed the guests. It was a grand occasion.

Meeting Details

After the meeting began, Mr. Zhang Shuiqi first reported on the progress of the preparation and collection work. Then, Mr. Ye Gongchuo, Chairman of the Committee, delivered a speech, stating that this photography submission was related to the future of the country and could not be done well by a small number of people. It was not easy to collect everything in Shanghai alone, and transportation was inconvenient and time was pressing. Therefore, he hoped that all experts would come to help devise sound methods to complete this important mission. Regarding the submissions, he should report to everyone that: (1) If the submitter cannot enlarge the photos themselves, they can submit the negatives to the travel service for free enlargement. The travel service will be responsible for returning the negatives in the future. (2) If the submitter enlarges the photos themselves, they do not need to mount or frame them. The travel service will handle everything to ensure that they are beautiful. (3) The travel service will not copy or print the submitter's negatives except to enlarge them for display in the United States. (4) If the submitter wants to sell the submissions, they can mark the Chinese currency price. After the sale, the submitter will receive the original price, minus a handling fee of one-tenth of the Chicago Exposition Preparatory Committee of the Ministry of Industry. (5) If the submitter has other questions that need to be discussed, they can write to the travel service at any time. Then, Zuo Gengsheng, Chen Wanli, Jiang Xiaojian, and others expressed their opinions and discussed the size of the submissions. After a collective decision, all submissions, whether they are famous scenic spots, historical sites, cultural relics, architecture, new construction, items for academic reference, customs, or art works, should be large in size (preferably 20x16) and not too small. It is hoped that submitters in various places will pay attention to this.

Recognition of Submissions

During the meeting, everyone recognized submissions. The maximum number of submissions recognized by one person was over 100, and the next highest was over a dozen. It was agreed that all submissions would be submitted to the travel service before January 5th. In addition, the photos taken by the National Travel Group of Liangyou will be provided as much as possible. All photos from the Times and China Pictorial magazines will also be submitted. Therefore, the results were very satisfactory. The company believes that the time for collection is extremely pressing and hopes that comrades in the photography community in various places will send their submissions to Shanghai as soon as possible to jointly participate in this grand event.

The Chinese Military Band, founded by the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, has been established for more than four months. Announcement from the Great Northern and Great Eastern Telegraph Companies

Amendments to the International Telegraph Regulations

The Great Northern and Great Eastern Telegraph Companies announce that, according to news received from their headquarters, representatives of various governments attending the International Telecommunications Conference in Madrid (the capital of Spain) have decided to amend certain articles of the current International Telegraph Regulations. Although detailed information has not yet been received, the following brief amendments, which are of the utmost importance, are believed to be of interest to you:

Code Telegrams:

Class A code words (code words with six to ten letters) will be cancelled. Code words are not allowed to exceed five letters, but there are no restrictions on the spelling of individual words.

Code telegrams are charged at 60% of the ordinary telegram rate. Telegrams exchanged within European countries are charged at 70% of the ordinary telegram rate.

If the telegram contains a mixture of clear language words and code words, it will be charged as a code telegram.

Clear language words are charged at one word for every five letters.

Each code telegram is charged at a minimum of five words.

Urgent Telegrams:

The price of urgent telegrams will be reduced from three times the ordinary full rate to two times (whether clear language or code).

Deferred, Night Letter, Day Letter, and Greetings Telegrams:

The text of these telegrams can be written in any language commonly used for ordinary clear language telegrams.

Except for the newly established regulations regarding urgent and letter telegrams, which will be implemented from April 1, 1933, the remaining newly established regulations will be implemented from January 1, 1934. Once the official text of the newly established regulations is received, detailed information will be sent to you. If you wish to forward the above news to other customers who send telegrams to various countries, please provide the customer's name and address in detail, and the companies will forward it accordingly. With best wishes,

Peng Sen, General Manager of the Far East, Great Northern Telegraph Company, Shanghai

Bo Leder, Manager of the China Division, Great Eastern Telegraph Company

Shanghai Municipal Council to Inspect School Hygiene

At the last meeting of the Education Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Council, the Director of the Health Department proposed a plan to conduct medical examinations in various schools. According to this plan, about 40,000 taels would need to be spent next year. Because the amount was quite large and it was a time of economic difficulty, a committee member suggested that this measure could be implemented gradually. At the beginning, it could be started in the schools directly managed by the bureau, especially the elementary schools directly managed by the bureau, and then extended to the subsidized schools. The Chairman of the Committee also said that it was necessary to conduct such inspections in schools. However, if the tax revenue next year and in the future does not increase, the Shanghai Municipal Council's regular expenses will also experience difficulties. Therefore, he could not help but hesitate about this plan, which requires a lot of expense. Then, the Director of the Health Department said that this inspection was originally a matter that should be handled by the municipal health authorities. If it is implemented, the expenses should be included under the Health Department. After discussion, all the committee members believed that this plan should be implemented, especially for the elementary schools directly managed by the bureau. However, they hoped that the financial situation next year would allow this plan or a revised plan to be implemented. However, this matter still needs to be sent to the Health Committee for consideration.

Shanghai News about the Paris Exposition

The Paris Exposition, which will be held next year, has now been scheduled to take place from May 13, 1933, to May 29th. This year, the area occupied by the exhibition was already quite large, with a hall of 120,000 square meters and other exhibition halls of 110,000 square meters. However, it was still insufficient, so an additional 10,000 square feet of space will be added for next year's exhibition. The main entrance of the venue has been the same for the past eight years, but it will be replaced with a new design next year, and a garden will be added. The number of exhibitors has been increasing year by year, reaching 7,850 this year, and it is expected that it will increase to 8,000 next year. Therefore, even during this period of economic panic, the affairs of the conference next year will not be affected and will be able to create a new era. It is heard that France and neighboring countries, to facilitate the travel of exhibitors and tourists, will reduce train and air travel expenses by 10% to 50% around May next year to show their preferential treatment. The office of the conference is located at Rue Notre Dame des Victories, Paris. Anyone wishing to participate can write to inquire about everything.

Shanghai Machine Association Condemns Zhao Jinji Factory for Falsely Claiming Membership

The Shanghai Machine-Made National Goods Factory Association sent a letter to the Zhao Jinji Thermos Factory, stating: "We have read the advertisement published by your factory in the 'Shen Bao' on the 13th of this month, which includes the words 'Member of the Shanghai Municipal Machine Association'. After careful examination of the membership application forms, your factory joined this association as a member in January 1929 and voluntarily announced its withdrawal in October of the same year. More than three years have passed, and your membership has long been terminated. How can you publish advertisements that falsely claim membership? Not only is this frivolous, it is also close to rumor-mongering and hinders the reputation of this association, which is illegal. Your recent application to join the association was rejected by the sixth meeting of the sixth session of the Executive Committee. A corresponding letter of warning is hereby prepared. Please pay close attention to avoid any inconvenience."

Alcohol Must Be Inspected First

Tang Haian, Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, and Luo Fude, Customs Commissioner, issued Joint Announcement No. 1263 yesterday, stating: "Regarding the matter of joint announcement, from now on, alcohol reported for import must be inspected by the Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry. Only after obtaining the certificate of conformity issued by the Inspection Bureau and sending it to the customs for verification will it be allowed to be released. For goods transported to ports where there is no Inspection Bureau, they should be imported through nearby ports where Inspection Bureaus have been established. It is hoped that all merchants will be informed of this. This announcement is hereby issued."

(Old Woman) In my opinion, a talent like the Xu fellow is good. He has an outstanding and refined appearance and is accomplished in literature. Matching him with our Hui'er would be a perfect pairing of a talented man and a beautiful woman, a harmonious union. It's a pity his family is poor; it's not a "suitable match." Unlike the Kang fellow, whose family is wealthy, which aligns with the ancient saying, "Marry your daughter three levels higher." A poor son-in-law is a disgrace! So, I think even though young Master Kang's talent doesn't match the Xu family's, his family is still quite suitable. If Hui'er marries him, she can live a life without worrying about food and clothing. (Old Man) No, no! I know this young Master Kang. Not only is his intelligence mediocre, but I've also heard he's arrogant and has a bad temper, ordering servants around. He's completely a spoiled young master. If Hui'er marries him, they might not have a harmonious marriage! Moreover, a friend told me that this young man, though young, is already addicted to opium. He's made a big mistake that will harm himself for life, and harm his wife and children. They say he spends four or five dollars a day on it, so even though his family has a large fortune, I don't approve of marrying a poppyhead! The Xu fellow is better. When it comes to wealth, although he's worlds apart from the Kang family, it's not like his family is completely destitute. As long as the child is ambitious, they won't be poor for life! (Old Woman) Old man, your idea is wrong. A person only needs to be well-fed and clothed in this world. Who cares about knowledge and learning? If we marry Hui'er to that poor Xu boy, we'll ruin her life. Do you think she'll resent us? It's better to marry her to the Kang fellow. When it comes to bad temper, I think other than poor boys, all the young masters from wealthy families are used to being pampered. They all throw tantrums. As long as Hui'er has skills, she can control him after marrying him. As for the opium addiction, that's even less of a concern. As the saying goes, "A rich man who smokes opium protects his family fortune." He has hundreds of thousands in assets. We should only worry about him not smoking opium, not worry about him spending money. With such a huge fortune, spending three or four dollars a day is nothing. Frankly, he won't smoke himself to poverty in his lifetime. So, I've decided to marry Hui'er to the Kang fellow to be a rich young mistress, and I don't want to send her to the poor Xu fellow to be a withered old woman! Old Master He's thinking was already outdated, and now, after his wife's words, his materialistic mindset was triggered, immediately forming a snobbish view of looking down on the poor and valuing the rich. He silently agreed with a soft, "Mmm..." (Old Woman) Since you agree too, when the matchmaker comes, we'll ask them to inform the groom's family to choose a date for the betrothal. Alas, He Huizhu's happiness, which her life depended on, the source of her fate, the marriage problem, was determined by her parents' outdated, money-worshipping, and despicable thinking, under the traditional, patriarchal values, and her fate was decided.

Meetings and Refreshments by Guang Yi

"Meetings" and "refreshments" may seem unrelated on the surface, but if you can observe them closely, I guarantee you'll immediately discover their interrelationship. I can't speak for other places, but in our school, every "meeting" is inseparable from "refreshments." As a rule, from the bell ringing to start the meeting until the closing remarks, there's always that "with delicious refreshments" bit. Frankly, if a meeting didn't have this item, perhaps besides the chairman and committee members, there wouldn't even be half a ghost there. This isn't an exaggeration; the facts tell us so. I remember that day was the day after the Lytton Report was published. The weather was very good, and the sun shone so brightly that every young person's veins seemed to be bursting. The chairman of the International Political Research Association, Mr. X, was really pitiful! In that hot sun, he had to run around, panting, to find the committee members and members to prepare for an in-depth study and discussion of the Lytton Report. Our chairman certainly had some research on the Lytton Report. I personally saw him take the spare time he had from studying movies last night to study the report, lighting a candle after the lights were turned off before going to sleep. He was truly pitiful! How diligent! The meeting time was 3:00 PM. The clever chairman had studied crowd psychology and knew that meetings and refreshments were closely related. Although there were no refreshments now, to ensure the smooth progress of the meeting, he wrote on the notice: "With delicious coffee and refreshments." This "coffee and refreshments" was even written in red, which is also the benefit of studying crowd psychology! The meeting was held. In addition to the committee members and members, non-members also participated. The crowd was so packed that it almost collapsed the XX Hall. Naturally, with refreshments, everything is easy to handle. But, unfortunately, it was a boast! A deceptive trick. Chairman: The meeting has been going on for a while, and I'm getting a little hungry, I think it's best to ask the chairman to speak first... Mr. X with thick lips stood up and said. That's right! Please, chairman, it's best to... The crowd echoed like a swarm of bees. Refreshments! Hurry! A burst of noise erupted. The poor chairman was really in a desperate situation, panting and saying: "Everyone, I'm sorry, I originally wanted to prepare refreshments today, but because there were not enough people, I didn't buy them, so I have to apologize. We'll have them next time!" What? No refreshments, are you kidding me? You... Mr. X, who came prepared to eat refreshments, shouted. XXX Refreshments Damn it XXX So, after a barrage of abuse, the crowd scattered in a puff of smoke. Only our poor chairman was left in the venue, staring blankly at the report. Later, he left too. So, this very lively meeting ended in a riot. Writing this, I think the intelligent reader will no longer deny that "meetings and refreshments" are unrelated. So, I would like to give a piece of advice: in any gathering in the future, if you want your members to attend, it's best if you can follow what I said above one by one. I guarantee you can get "young and old together," perhaps even "all the wise men gathered." There is certainly no doubt about this. Intelligent readers, right?

Be Careful of Fire? By Zhang Yiping

As the year draws to a close, the northwest wind every night carries the slogan "Be careful of fire." A family that manufactures children's fireworks moved into the house next door. The people in the alley warned the second landlord not to let this family move in. However, the high rent strangled the second landlord's throat, and in a "compromise," the workshop finally settled down. Who knew that within less than ten days, a fire broke out? The second landlord got a taste of prison life, which was deserved. To whom should we claim compensation for the losses from being burned? It was lunchtime, and the children were jumping on the benches, welcoming the fragrant bucket of plain rice being brought out of the kitchen. Suddenly, a shrill cry entered my ears, followed by the sound of chaotic police sirens. I hurriedly opened the door. The people in the alley, carrying the old and supporting the young, were desperately running out. The young and strong were also carrying boxes of miscellaneous items. I looked up and saw sparks rising from the roof of the house next door. As I turned back into the house, there was loud crying and screaming inside. Outside, the police sirens were blowing chaotically. Suddenly, there was a crashing sound, as if a wall next door had collapsed. The people in the house were all panicked. Some dragged blankets, and some even squeezed towards the gate holding bowls of rice. Because our family was at the end of the alley, after the fire next door raged, there was no way to escape with our lives. I forced myself to calm down and told my family to escape first. I ran upstairs. I don't know where the divine power came from, but I broke the lock on the box under the bed and carried the small box that our family thought was valuable. As I ran out into the courtyard, the flames from our main building were like millions of snakes, choosing people to devour through the cracks in the windows. I rushed out of the gate, and sparks were already on my body. At this time, the fire trucks had arrived. The alley was immediately closed to pedestrians. I had no choice but to take refuge in a Shikumen house in the front alley. Almost all the people in the alley were acquaintances. I jumped onto their drying platform and shouted to my family standing in the open air outside the alley, afraid that they would think I had been buried in the fire. Now that I couldn't leave, I leaned on the drying platform to watch them put out the fire. But at this time, the wind was strong, and in an instant, our house was on fire. The firefighters held the hoses and watered it down. At the same time, they used axes to tear down the nearby walls to prevent the fire from spreading. An hour later, the fire was completely extinguished. A total of five houses were burned. I looked at my own house, mostly collapsed in the rubble. All the remaining items were split and smashed by the firefighters, as if they were searching for something, rummaging everywhere. I leaned on the drying platform and looked at the men, women, old, and young standing in the middle of the street, with nowhere to go, and couldn't help but burst into tears. The second landlord, for the sake of a few more dollars in rent each month, moved in a dangerous tenant, causing the people in these five houses to be displaced (later learned that two people had been buried in the fire) and had gone to the police station to taste the taste of prison life. But the firefighters should not take advantage of the fire to rob, searching as much as possible for the remaining items. Do you know how the victims standing in the street are grateful for your firefighting? But can you say a word? I hope the authorities will consider the suffering of the victims and provide the firefighters with considerable improvements. If this thing can be published, I hope that every time I hear the slogan "Be careful of fire" in the northwest wind, everyone will carefully check the places where fire can easily be left behind.

Novel: Writing a Letter to a Friend's Wife (Continuation 14) By Qin Shouou

At this time, my soul is very happy, and my spirit is also very excited; because when the train passed Xiaguan, I had already used five aspirin tablets to solve my fever. Last night, I ate three steaks by myself; however, I didn't feel any taste, like chewing on three blocks of wood. I am working so hard to add to my meals, hoping that before leaving the pass, I will have fully recovered my inherent health and lively spirit. At the very least, when I step into the ranks of the Volunteer Army, I will definitely not even have the strength to fight the Japanese beast soldiers! The motive for my departure this time has been told to you as much as possible 丨 I am sacrificing myself to protect your reputation, as well as the happiness of Dajing and Xiaoqiangwei; of course, it cannot be said to be for patriotism. However, the reason is not just that simple: If I really didn't have some will to protect the motherland, wouldn't it be easiest and most straightforward to sacrifice myself by jumping into the Huangpu River? Why would I have to go to Guanwai in such a roundabout way to seek sacrifice? Alas! Beautiful little piggy! You may be very vague about the real situation of our great Republic of China, right? This can't be blamed on you either. Originally, the female citizens of the Great Republic of China were inherently a machine for selling foreign goods: besides studying decoration, who has ever paid attention to the country? Maybe they don't even know what year of the Republic of China it is! Now, let me tell you! Little brother! Our great Republic of China is really suffering from the third stage of lung disease! If the government is still so chaotic and muddled, and the common people are still so extravagant and dissolute, then within ten years, if the national emblem of the blue sky and white sun can still fly in the sunlight, I am willing to turn into a turtle in my next life for you to see! Just take the January 28th Shanghai Incident as an example. If the Japanese were so tyrannical, unreasonable, and contemptuous of friendly nations, and performed such a farce in the territory of other countries, I dare guarantee that on the morning of January 29th, the young people and adults in the surrounding area would definitely immediately gather at the battlefield. No matter how sharp the Japanese beast soldiers' cannons and how active the planes were, they would also take courage and stand on the front line; and they didn't necessarily have to get guns and cannons, even a bayonet or a wooden stick could be used to fight a desperate battle with the Japanese beast soldiers one after another, chilling the enemy's courage! However, when Wusong, Jiangwan, and Zhabei were being attacked, burned, massacred, and raped one after another, the young people and adults of our great Republic of China fled to the concessions under the protection of imperialism; gathered together to watch movies, patronize prostitutes, play mahjong, play poker, and even many more shameless guys were having so much fun that they forgot the time, lingering on the streets past 11 o'clock, and being caught in large numbers by foreigners and taken to the police station. How can a nation so shameless and bloodless survive in an era where it will perish if it does not compete?

Film Special: Strange Overseas News: The Mystery of Paul Bern's Suicide By Lin

Paul Bern, the husband of blonde actress Jean Harlow, shot himself in the head with a gun just two months after marrying Jean. When this news came out, not only was Hollywood shocked, but the whole world was also very surprised. Even the Associated Press sent several special telegrams about it. However, the cause of Paul's death is still unknown. It is said that Jean herself also felt baffled, or knew but kept it a secret. Therefore, people only know that Paul committed suicide, but they cannot find out the reason for his suicide, and this mystery will probably be buried underground with Paul forever. Recently, a Hollywood astrologer, Sareos, claimed to have discovered the reason for Paul's suicide. Sareos is not only an expert in astrological exploration but is also a great mental scholar. He said that he knew about this months before Paul and Jean got married. One day Paul came to visit this great astrologer. It is said that at this time, the root of suicide had already been planted in Paul's mind. Paul was very kind and had a quiet mind, but all kinds of fantasies occupied it. Paul's thinking was very inclined to theology, and he deeply believed that doing good deeds in this life would definitely bring good results in the next life. Paul deeply loved Jean, and no one could stop his spirit of sacrifice. He firmly believed that Jean would become a great actress in the future, but she has not yet gained enough experience, and her talent is still asleep. She needs a great stimulus to awaken her talent. But if a huge scar can be left in her mind, it will definitely enable her to turn the experiences of joys and sorrows in her life into moving works, and Jean's future may be as famous as Duse and Bernhardt. Paul had told Sareos about this idea and claimed that his mission in this world had been completed, etc. After the news of Paul's suicide came out, Sareos sighed deeply, so he determined that Paul's suicide was actually for Jean's future, and he had made this great selfless sacrifice. Sareos's spiritualism has always been believed in by Hollywood, so his conclusion is also believed by the public. Tonight, Santa Claus came from the Arctic Ocean in a reindeer sleigh to various countries. You don't need to go to the company to buy it; I'll send you one first.

Random Thoughts on the Style of the Film Industry By Huizun

A writer has his style; an artist also has a style. Similarly, a movie actor, a bright star, also has a star's style. Janet Gaynor's petite and exquisite; McDonald's magnificent; Norma Shearer's charming to the bone; Seiffert's dashing and handsome; Van Fairbanks' heroic and strong: ... countless Hollywood stars, they all have their own styles. Our Chinese stars don't seem to give us such a concept. For example, if you ask: What is Hu Die's style? What is Ruan Lingyu's style? What are the styles of Jin Yan, Zheng Xiaoqiu, Gong Jianong, Chen Yumei, etc.? Then it is difficult for us to give an answer, because they can play any role, rural girl, modern young lady, student celebrity, promiscuous starlet, gentleman aristocrat, hawker, hero, playboy, everything is possible. Therefore, we have no way to appreciate their style. If something becomes specialized, it is easy to excel; if a star forms a style, it is also easy to show its strengths. But to create a style, you must have extremely precise observation. Directors need to see the talent of actors and give them appropriate roles in the script. The actors themselves also choose roles in the script that suit their talents. In this way, the style of a star can also be created.

Yang Liuqing's Death By Jibing

Ms. Yang was a daughter from a prominent Hangzhou family. Due to frustration in love, she once attempted suicide but was rescued. Later, she quietly came to Shanghai to join the film industry. She first entered Tianxing but was unsuccessful, and then was introduced by Mr. Xie Qingping to join Dazhong. This time, she went to Suzhou with Dazhong to shoot on location. Unexpectedly, this beautiful woman died in the "Lone Army" battle. The last happy gathering before Dazhong left Shanghai was at Xinya. Ms. Yang and twelve other actors and staff members of the company exchanged drinks and laughed happily. Before the halfway point of the banquet, a newly arrived actress suddenly arrived, bringing the number of attendees to thirteen. At that time, Wei Xiubao had a phone call saying that he would come soon, but he did not arrive until the end of the banquet. Therefore, the number thirteen could not be changed. Later, Yang Liuqing was injured at Tianping Mountain and was carried to the Gengsheng Hospital by members of the company. Guan Shi diagnosed and treated her. Zhou Shixun was the first to discover that the number of the ward was also thirteen. Because the West considers thirteen to be very unlucky, he remained silent and did not speak. Who knew that this double thirteen would really be an ominous omen?

A Suggestion to Add a 7:00 PM Show By Fei

Most movie theaters now, except for a very few, only show three screenings a day, roughly at 3:00, 5:30, and 9:15. I think this is extremely inconvenient for the audience, especially now in winter. For example, the 9:15 show ends at around 11:00 PM. The audience runs from the warm theater to the cold street, exposed to the cold wind, which must be unbearable. Also, for example, people who go to the 5:30 show often have to sacrifice dinner, which is the case for us students. Therefore, I propose that many movie theaters can add a 7:00 PM show. Then we can go after dinner, and the show won't end too late, which is very convenient. It will probably also be better for the business of the movie theaters!

My Experience Kissing on the Silver Screen By Kang Bing

Since making films, Neil Hamilton has kissed sixty-seven women, which means he has learned sixty-seven ways to kiss. He is very proficient in this way. According to him, among the many women he has kissed, Joan Crawford is the most tactful, and Helen Hayes is the most genuine. Neil Hamilton said that kissing is not an easy thing to do. When he was performing with Norma Shearer in Strangers May Kiss, he was very worried because Norma was his master Thalberg's wife! So he was very restrained and dared not be too presumptuous. However, he was ridiculed by Norma for this. He said, "Kissing Joan Crawford is the most pleasant. She is very tactful, and she trembles passionately when she kisses her. This seems close to licentiousness, but Joan's attitude is open and unquestionable." He also said, "Kissing Mary Brian gives people another kind of feeling. She is very sincere and has no hypocrisy at all." Regarding Helen Hayes, he said, "She is the most genuine. Her true feelings are simply exhilarating. On the other hand, with Bebe Daniels, there is very little true feeling when kissing her. She is neither as tactful as Joan Crawford nor does she have the true feelings of Helen Hayes. Her kissing is completely dramatic." Mrs. Hamilton is a generous and happy woman. She sees her husband embracing and kissing beautiful women on the screen, and she is not jealous at all. If your aunt is a very fat woman and you give her a girl's bodice, you can imagine how she would react when she received the gift.

Lianhua Suffers Political Restraint Again By Ming

The "Three Modern Women," which has been promoted for a long time, has a very strong stimulating effect in the last scene of the major strike. Fearing that it would be disapproved by the Central Film Censorship Committee, eight hundred feet were cut, and the last scene was rewritten and reshot in secret, resulting in the relocation of the set. A large section of the previous four hundred actors was completely sacrificed. It has now been sent to Beijing for inspection and approval, and it will be shown from the 29th, it is said.

A Local News Item: A Future Star By Qingxia

Xia Peizhu, she is a lively and clever girl; she is twenty-eight years old, has a beautiful appearance, and is very similar to Hu Die; she has a gentle temperament and is amiable. She is currently studying at the French Concession Chinese Children's Public School. She is intelligent by nature and usually silent and quiet. Since entering the school, she has never asked for a day off, nor has she ever been late, except when it was unavoidable. We can imagine how much she values her studies; and she is very frugal and has none of the habits of modern people. Who is she? She is Xia Peizhen's younger sister—Xia Peizhu. She is very interested in movies; she also hopes that she can appear on the screen immediately; because her sister Xia Peizhen, whenever she returns from shooting on location in other places, always talks about how excellent and moving the scenery there is; and at the end of the month, she also brings home a large roll of banknotes—salary—so in a corner of her mind, she has imprinted a deep impression: "Filming movies is such an interesting thing!" She has asked her family several times to allow her to make movies, but she has been repeatedly rejected; she feels very frustrated and unhappy that she cannot fulfill her long-cherished wish. Recently, it is said that she has obtained the permission of her family and will be allowed to engage in film after graduating from the Chinese Children's Public School, so she has been very happy recently and cannot stop smiling.

Film Essay: The Honor of Being "Overwhelmed by Favor" By Chen DabeI

In the film set, before each shot, the director must first order the actors to practice it once. After he is satisfied, he will issue the order to start the camera. Almost this procedure is the same in any film set. The director's temperaments are different. But for expressions that are considered unsatisfactory, no director can vaguely order the photographer to start shooting. The director thinks that your expression is not suitable, and clearly points out your unsuitable points. If you still don't know what your expression is like at that time, the simplest, clumsiest, and most common method is to continuously change various expressions for the director to choose one. Every time you try one, the director shakes his head, and you feel very ashamed. Fortunately, the director is satisfied with the last one. And you also feel "overwhelmed by favor." But when the lighting engineer has adjusted the lights and the photographer is cranking the camera, a muscle on your face suddenly dances involuntarily, and your mind seems to be suddenly oppressed, and the expression you make is a hundred and eighty yards away from the expression you just tried for the director and was considered satisfactory. So the director suddenly orders the camera to stop, all the lights go out. What do you think at that time? Whose fault is it? The director blames you. Who do you blame?

Yesterday's Joint Meeting of the Abolish War Association

Discussing How to Stop the Sichuan-Guizhou Civil War

Resolutions Made and Telegraphed to the Central Government

The General Association of the Abolish Civil War League convened a meeting yesterday in Shanghai, gathering representatives from various Sichuan and Guizhou hometown associations to discuss ways to stop the civil war. Representatives from the Sichuan and Guizhou hometown associations, as well as standing committee members of the Abolish Civil War League, including Wang Xiaolai, Lin Kanghou, Du Yuesheng, Qian Xinzhi, Xu Jiyi, Chen Zheqing, and Yan Esheng, totaling over fifty people, attended. After the meeting began, Wang Xiaolai, the current standing committee member of the League, presided over it. First, the chairman reported the purpose of convening the meeting today. Then, Lin Kanghou reported on the petition to the Third Plenary Session in Beijing. Next, Secretary-General Yan Esheng reported on the recent situation of the League's efforts to stop the Sichuan-Guizhou war. Following that, Qiu Zhizhong, Zhong Hangsu, Huang Fogong, Yin Ziqin, Qian Xinzhi, Li Chongpu, Liu Qinghuai, Peng Zexi, Kang Xuanyi, and others successively expressed their opinions on the Sichuan situation. Afterwards, Wan Weizeng and Xiao Haiyuan expressed their opinions on the Guizhou situation. After detailed discussions among the attendees, the chairman summarized everyone's opinions, and the secretary-general drafted a telegram, which was passed on the spot and sent. The original telegram is as follows: To the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Military Affairs Commission, and the Ministry of Military Affairs, Nanjing: Our association invited representatives from Sichuan's hometown, academic, and business groups in Shanghai to jointly discuss and unanimously resolved the following: (1) Request the Central Government to strictly order the Sichuan army to cease fire immediately. (2) Request the Central Government to promptly form a Sichuan Affairs Reorganization Committee, with Zhang Qun as the chairman and with central officials and representatives of professional civilians from both inside and outside Sichuan as members; incumbent military personnel should absolutely not participate. (3) Request the Central Government to authorize the Reorganization Committee with full authority to reorganize the Sichuan army, reassign them to recover lost territories, suppress bandits, and defend the borders; simultaneously, reorganize civil finance, local militias, and party affairs; and assign local militias to take charge of public security throughout the province, and plan to convene a provincial people's congress to discuss long-term peace and stability measures. (4) Request the Central Government to strictly prohibit the entry of military supplies into Sichuan. (5) Request the Central Government to investigate and punish the instigators of the Sichuan war and issue a pre-declaration stating that those who refuse to comply with the Reorganization Committee's decisions will be severely punished without any leniency. The above five points are all urgent measures to stop the Sichuan war. As for stopping the civil war in Guizhou Province, we request the Central Government to transfer Wang's troops away from Guizhou and assign them to bandit suppression or recovering lost territories, and not to allow incumbent military personnel to govern the province, strictly implement military-civilian separation, and we also pray for prompt adoption and implementation, without delay, awaiting orders urgently, The General Association of the Abolish Civil War League bows respectfully.

The National Lawyers Association's Telegram Regarding Opinions on the Resumption of Sino-Soviet Diplomatic Relations

Regarding the resumption of Sino-Soviet diplomatic relations, the National Lawyers Association specifically issued a telegram yesterday, the original text is as follows: To all newspapers and people's organizations nationwide: England and France condone Japan, the authority of the League of Nations has been completely swept away, and international treaties no longer exist. Our government, at a time when there is no justice to be found in the world, decisively resumed diplomatic relations with Soviet Russia to promote peace and prosperity in the Far East. Its intention is indeed gratifying. However, international relations only consider interests and do not speak of sentiment. Friends in the morning may be enemies in the evening, and changes are unpredictable. Therefore, those who are good at planning for the country value the way of befriending neighbors, but even more so value the way of self-strengthening. If one cannot strengthen oneself and hopes for the generosity of neighbors, this is certainly impossible. Nowadays, the people of our country take the resumption of Sino-Soviet diplomatic relations as a cause for celebration. I believe that having one more allied country in the international arena is certainly a fortunate thing. However, if our country's politics remains unreformed, its economy continues to decline, and even if superiors and subordinates are estranged, and internal divisions are as severe as fire and water, then what we hope from neighboring countries today will still be what we despair of from neighboring countries in the future, and perhaps even more than just despair. I hope that all my good citizens will strive to save themselves and not rely on others in the slightest. This would be truly fortunate. Liu Liumin, Jiang Yong, Yan Yinwu, Dai Tianqiu, Liu Zhe, Standing Committee Members of the All China Lawyers Association, bows respectfully.

Post Office Issues Commemorative Stamps for President Tan

Starting from January 9th, 1933

According to the post office, the commemorative stamps for President Tan (divided into denominations of 2 cents, 5 cents, 25 cents, and 1 yuan) have been scheduled to be issued on January 9th, 1933, the day of the completion of President Tan's Memorial Hall and Mausoleum Project, by post offices and agencies, and will be available until the end of June of the same year. If, when purchasing, you wish to have the post office's date stamp applied, the post office can also do so. These stamps will have a general usage period of six months after the end of the issuance period, that is, from July 1st to December 31st, 1933. During this general usage period, they can still be affixed to postal items as postage, and can also be exchanged at post offices for ordinary stamps of the same value. If it reaches January 1st, 1934, they will no longer be applicable and will not be allowed to be exchanged, in order to show restrictions. As for these commemorative stamps issued in Xinjiang and Yunnan, they have all been separately overprinted with the words "For Use in Xinjiang Province" and "For Use in Yunnan Province." In addition to being sold in those respective regions, the Nanjing, Shanghai, Hankou, Beiping, and Panyu postal administrations have also issued a small number for sale, for collectors to purchase nearby (all unused with postmarks). However, the postal area for which these overprinted stamps are valid is limited to what is clearly stated on the stamp surface. If you wish to purchase stamps with the Di Hua (Xinjiang) and Kunming (Yunnan) postmarks, in addition to purchasing from the Xinjiang and Yunnan postal administrations, you can also have them purchased on your behalf through the Beiping Postal Administration.

Japanese Residents Present Detailed Chinese Map

Visiting Qiyakou to Observe Our Waterways

Workers at the Great Shanghai Rubber Factory Resume Work

Waiting for Mediation of the Conditions

More than 200 male and female workers at the Great Shanghai Rubber Factory on Datupu Bridge and Xietu Road announced a strike due to their request for double pay for December not being met. They also put forward nine conditions. After persuasion from party and government organs yesterday, they all resumed work. The details are recorded below:

(Petitioning the Party and Government) The striking workers sent representatives Sun Yuanqun, Chen Heshang, Wang Xianfu, and others, more than ten people in total, to the city party headquarters to petition, along with Chu Chengdong and Lu Ganhuа, the directors of the First District Rubber Workers' Union, requesting a speedy mediation. Li Weixiong of the Civil Training Section met with them and indicated that he had received the conditions put forward by the workers and agreed to mediate them, but hoped that the workers would resume work immediately. Then the representatives went to the Social Affairs Bureau to petition, where they were met by Zhu Guilin of the Third Section, who also agreed to investigate and handle the matter after investigation.

(Persuasion to Resume Work) After receiving the workers' petition, the party and government organs sent Li Weixiong from the city party headquarters and Zhu Guilin from the Social Affairs Bureau to mediate at 3 pm, and persuaded the workers to resume work first and wait for the conditions to be mediated in accordance with the law. However, the workers refused to resume work because the factory posted a notice setting a deadline for dismissal, which they considered an intentional pressure tactic. The party and government representatives ordered the factory to automatically withdraw the notice, and all the workers then complied with the persuasion and resumed work at 4 pm.

Workers at the Sanyou Factory Attacked Again

Two Workers Seriously Stabbed with Knives

The Union Petitions the Municipal Government to Demand Investigation

The labor dispute at the Sanyou Industrial Company in Yinxiang Port, Pudong has been dragging on for a year and has not yet been resolved. The workers are still living in the factory, waiting for a judicial resolution. On the 15th of this month, workers Wu Songshou and others were attacked. At around 11:00 pm the day before yesterday, the workers in the factory were sound asleep, when a number of people broke into the factory through the back door in the dark, holding iron rulers and sharp weapons, and rushed to the workers' bedrooms, attacking anyone they encountered. All ten workers living in the factory were awakened from their sleep and fled in a panic. Worker Xu Dejing was stabbed twice in the leg, and blood flowed like a waterfall. Zhang Baozhong was stabbed three times in the right arm and leg and was seriously injured. The Fifth District Fourth Precinct and the security team stationed in the factory immediately sent armed police to hunt down the attackers, but the perpetrators had already fled upon hearing the news and could not be apprehended. The injured were taken to Yangshupu Sacred Heart Hospital for treatment. The Seventh District Cotton Weaving Workers' Union convened an emergency meeting of workers at the factory yesterday morning and decided to send representatives Fan Bangyong, Wang Chuncheng, Sun Shouming, and Leng Shimо to the municipal government with a document to petition, requesting a thorough investigation and assistance with their livelihood. After the municipal government received the workers' petition, it immediately replied, "Your petition has been noted. Yang Changlin and others dared to carry weapons in the dead of night and break into the factory to kill workers, causing Xu Dejing and Zhang Baozhi to be seriously injured. This is extremely illegal. The Public Security Bureau is ordered to strictly investigate and arrest the perpetrators. The district office is ordered to do its best to protect the safety of the workers. In addition to the order, the union is notified and allowed to request the local district office to send a team to protect them at any time to prevent accidents. This is the approval, Mayor Wu Tiecheng."

Ministry of Industries Will Investigate Zhejiang Industries

The National Industrial Survey of the Ministry of Industries, after being ordered to be handled by the International Trade Bureau, commenced on August 1st. Currently, the survey of Jiangsu Province and other provinces has been fully completed and is being typeset. The Jiangsu Province Industrial Records will be published in one month. The entire book is divided into eleven volumes, one hundred and twenty chapters, and approximately 800,000 words. Currently, the bureau has decided to continue surveying Zhejiang in accordance with the first phase of the survey plan for five provinces approved by the Executive Yuan, and will begin soon. Hou Houpei, the director of the investigation, is said to have been dispatched to Hangzhou yesterday to contact various parties in the provincial government.
